    It shall be unlawful for any person to harass, threaten, harm, damage or otherwise penalize any individual, group or business because such individual, group or business has complied with the provisions of this article, because such individual, group or business has exercised the rights established under this article, or enjoyed the benefits of this article, or made a charge, testified or assisted in any investigation, or in any proceeding hereunder or made any report to the administrator. 
(Code 1981, § 16.50; Ord. of 8-9-1993) 
Sec. 12-30. - Cooperation with the Secretary of Housing and Urban Development. 
    The City Administrator and the City Attorney are authorized to cooperate with the Secretary of Housing and Urban Development and the U.S. Attorney General pursuant to the provisions of the Fair Housing Act, 42 USC 3601 et seq. (2006) and Texas Fair Housing Act, V.T.C.A., Property Code § 301.001 et seq., and may render such services to the Secretary as they shall deem appropriate to further the policies of this article. 
(Code 1981, § 16.51; Ord. of 8-9-1993) 
Sec. 12-31. - Education and public information. 
    In order to further the objectives of this article, the administrator may conduct educational and public information programs. 
(Code 1981, § 16.52; Ord. of 8-9-1993) 
Sec. 12-32. - Penalty. 
(a)  Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties of section 1-12. Each day a violation continues after passage of 75 days from date of the filing of the initial complaint with the administrator shall constitute a separate and distinct offense. 
(b)  Any person violating any provision of this article may be enjoined by order of a court of competent jurisdiction, and this remedy is in addition to any other penalty provision. 
(Code 1981, § 16.53; Ord. of 8-9-1993) 
Chapter 14 - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Emergency management, V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 418; municipal programs, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 418.103. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 14-1-14-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MUNICIPAL DISASTER EMERGENCY SERVICES COMMITTEE 

Sec. 14-19. - Creation of disaster committee. 
    There is hereby created the municipal disaster emergency services committee of the City which shall consist of the following: 
(1)  The mayor who shall serve as chairperson of the committee, and who shall also be known as municipal disaster coordinator. 
(2)  The assistant disaster coordinator of the City, who shall be charged with the preparation of a disaster services plan for the City, together with such other duties as the coordinator may prescribe. The assistant coordinator shall be appointed by and hold the position at the pleasure of the City Council. The assistant coordinator shall serve as vice-chairperson of the municipal disaster emergency services committee of the City. 
(3)  The directors of divisions and chiefs of services of such divisions as may be provided for by resolution by the City Council or by directive of the municipal disaster coordinator. 
(4)  Representatives from civic, business, industry, labor, veterans, professional or other groups, to be selected and appointed by the City Council. 
(Code 1981, § 9.100; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-20. - Authority of committee. 
    The authority of the municipal disaster emergency services committee shall include the recommendation for adoption by the City Council of a disaster services plan for the City, and the recommendation for adoption by the City Council of any and all mutual aid plans and agreements which are deemed essential for the implementation of such disaster services plan. The authority of said committee shall also include the making of a survey of the availability of existing personnel, equipment, supplies and services which could be used during an emergency, as provided for herein, as well as a continuing study of the need for amendments and improvements in the disaster services plan adopted by the City Council. The disaster emergency services committee shall meet upon the call of either the chairperson or vice-chairperson. 
(Code 1981, § 9.101; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-21. - Joined with county. 
    The mayor is hereby authorized to join with the county judge and the mayors of the other cities in said county in the formation of a disaster emergency services council for the county and shall have the authority to cooperate in the formation of a disaster services plan and in the appointment of a disaster director for the county as well as all other powers necessary to participate in a county-wide program of disaster services insofar as said program may affect the City. 
(Code 1981, § 9.102; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-22. - Office of disaster coordinator. 
(a)  The office of municipal disaster coordinator is hereby created. The municipal disaster coordinator shall have the authority to request the declaration of the existence of an emergency by the City Council or by higher authority. In the event it is deemed necessary to declare without delay the existence of an emergency, the coordinator may do so, if the City Council is not in session, but such action shall be subject to confirmation by the City Council at its next meeting. 
(b)  The authority of the municipal disaster coordinator shall include the following: 
(1)  The control and direction of the actual operation or training of the disaster services organization of the City; 
(2)  The determination of all questions of authority and responsibility that may arise within the disaster services organization of the City; 
(3)  The maintenance of necessary liaison with other municipal, district, state, county, regional, federal or other disaster services organization; 
(4)  The marshaling, after declaration of an emergency as provided for in subsection (a) of this section, of all necessary personnel, equipment or supplies from any department of the City to aid in the carrying out of the disaster services plan; 
(5)  The issuance of all necessary proclamations as to the existence of an emergency and the immediate operational effectiveness of the disaster services plan; 
(6)  The issuance of reasonable rules, regulations or directives which are necessary for the protection of life and property in the City, such rules and regulations as and when promulgated shall be filed in the office of the City Clerk and shall receive widespread publicity unless publicity will be of aid and comfort to the enemy; 
(7)  The supervision of the drafting and execution of mutual aid agreements, in cooperation with the representatives of the state and of other local political subdivisions of the state, and the drafting and execution, if deemed desirable, of an agreement with the county in which the City is located and with other municipalities within the county, for the countywide coordination of efforts in disaster services; 
(8)  The supervision of and final authorization for the procurement of all necessary supplies and equipment, including acceptance of private contributions; and 
(9)  The authorizing or agreements, after approval of the City Attorney, for the use of private property for public shelter and other purposes. 
(Code 1981, § 9.103; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-23. - Disaster workers. 
    The operational disaster services organization of the City shall consist of the officers and employees of the City designated by the municipal disaster coordinator as well as all volunteer municipal workers. The functions and duties of this organization shall be distributed among such divisions, services and special staff as the City Council shall prescribe by resolution or the municipal disaster coordinator shall provide by directive. Any such resolution or directive shall set forth the form of organization, establish and designate divisions and services, assign functions, duties and powers, and designate officers and employees to carry out the provisions of this article. Insofar as possible, the form of organization, titles and terminology shall conform to the recommendations of the state defense and disaster relief council of the state and of the federal government. 
(Code 1981, § 9.104; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-24. - Controlling effect. 
    At all times when the orders, rules and regulations made and promulgated pursuant to this article shall be in effect, they shall supersede all existing ordinances, orders, rules and regulations insofar as the latter may be inconsistent therewith. This article shall not be construed so as to conflict with any state or federal statute or with any military or naval order, rule or regulation. 
(Code 1981, § 9.105; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-25. - Limitation of liability. 
    This article is an exercise by the City of its governmental functions for the protection of the public peace, health and safety, and neither the City, the agents and representatives of said City, or any individual, receiver, firm, partnership, corporation, association or trustee or any of the agents thereof, in good faith carrying out, complying with or attempting to comply with any order, rule or regulation promulgated pursuant to the provisions of this article shall be liable for any damage sustained to persons as the result of said activity. The failure of any office or committee hereby created to prepare any report or plan or to perform any purely administrative task shall not be grounds for imposition of civil liability against such officer or committee member, either directly or indirectly. Any person owning or controlling real estate or other premises who voluntarily and without compensation grants to the City a license or privilege, or otherwise permits the City to inspect, designate and use the whole or any part or parts of such real estate or premises for the purpose of sheltering persons during an actual, impending or practice enemy attack shall, together with any successors in interest, not be civilly liable for the death of, or injury to, any person on or about such real estate or premises under such license, privilege or other permission or for loss of, or damage to, the property of such person. 
(Code 1981, § 9.106; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-26. - Restriction on expenditures. 
    No person shall have the right to expend any public funds of the City in carrying out any disaster services activity authorized by this article without prior approval by the City Council, nor shall any person have any right to bind the City by contract, agreement or otherwise without prior and specific approval of the City Council. 
(Code 1981, § 9.107; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-27. - Unlawful acts. 
(a)  Any unauthorized person who shall operate a siren or other device so as to simulate a warning signal or the termination of a warning, shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this article and shall be subject to the penalties imposed by this article. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person willfully to obstruct, hinder or delay any member of the disaster services organization in the enforcement of any rule or regulation issued pursuant to this article or to commit any act forbidden by any rules or regulation issued pursuant to the authority contained in this article. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to wear, carry or display any emblem, insignia or any other means of identification as a member of the disaster services organization of the City, unless authority to do so has been granted to such person by the proper officials. 
(Code 1981, § 9.108; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Sec. 14-28. - Penalties. 
    Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties of section 1-12. 
(Code 1981, § 9.109; Ord. of 10-9-1977) 
Chapter 16 - ENVIRONMENT AND HEALTH[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Sanitation and environmental quality, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 341 et seq.; natural resources, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code ch. 1 et seq.; parks and wildlife, V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 16-1-16-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - UNSANITARY BUILDINGS AND LOTS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Protection of public health, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 122.005; sanitation, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 342; litter abatement, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 365; minimum standards of sanitation and health protection measures, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 341; general enforcement authority of municipality, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 54; regulation of businesses and occupations, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 215. 

Sec. 16-19. - Unsanitary and unsightly places. 
    The City Council or its designated agent shall have the power to: 
(1)  Require the filling up, drainage, or other appropriate remedial action of any lots, grounds, or yards, or any other places in the City, which shall be unwholesome or have stagnant water therein, or from any other cause be in such condition as to be liable to produce disease; 
(2)  To regulate or require the filling up, altering or repairing of all sinks and the removal of all privies and directing the mode and material for cleaning and disinfecting the same, and for cleaning any house, building, lot, yard, or ground from filth, carrion, or any other impure or unwholesome matter of any kind; and 
(3)  To require the person owning any premises, lot or location within the City to maintain grass and weeds (as defined in section 16-20), and to keep the same free from abandoned property, debris, junk, litter or rubbish (as defined in section 16-21) as well as any other objectionable or unsightly or unsanitary matter of whatever nature. 
(Code 1981, § 9.1; Ord. No. 05-05; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.1, 7-10-2007; Ord. No. 11-08, § 2, 12-13-2011) 
Sec. 16-20. - Maintenance standards for weeds and grass. 
    It is a violation of this article for the owner of any possessory interest in any real property located within the City to permit either grass exceeding 12 inches in height or weeds exceeding 12 inches in height to exist on 60 percent or more of that portion of any residential lot that is not covered by a permanent structure. 
(Code 1981, § 9.2; Ord. No. 05-05; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.2, 7-10-2007) 
Sec. 16-21. - Maintenance standards for abandoned property, debris, junk, litter and rubbish. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Abandoned property means personal property over which the owner appears to have relinquished its claim of ownership or entitlement. Abandonment may be proved by circumstantial evidence, such as location, condition and length of time in either. 
    Debris means the remains of anything broken down or destroyed. 
    Junk means abandoned material or objects. 
    Litter means rubbish which has been scattered about. 
    Rubbish means useless waste or rejected matter. 
(b)  Unlawful activities enumerated. 
(1)  It is unlawful for any person, including the owner of real property located within the City limits, or organization to permit abandoned property, debris, junk, rubbish or litter or any of the following items to remain on real property located within the City limits, when visible from the public right-of-way or a neighboring real property: 
a.  Broken, inoperable, or discarded household furnishings, appliances, machines, tools, cans, containers, boxes and cartons, lawn maintenance equipment, play equipment, toys, grills, camper parts and similar items; 
b.  Used or discarded building materials; 
c.  Items stored on rooftops or front, back or side porches of buildings; 
d.  Damaged merchandise; 
e.  Used, discarded or broken automotive parts or equipment; or 
f.  Any materials that tend by decay to become putrid or to provide harborage for rodents and other vectors. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or deposit any rubbish, junk or debris upon any vacant lot or private property within the City. 
(Code 1981, § 9.3; Ord. No. 05-05; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.3, 7-10-2007; Ord. No. 11-08, § 2, 12-13-2011) 
Sec. 16-22. - Notice of violation. 
(a)  One time during each calendar year, the City Council or its designated agent shall personally notify, in writing, the owner of any premises or lots described in section 16-19 that a violation of this article appears to exist on his/her property (which property shall be identified in the notice). 
(b)  Such written notice may be served by: 
(1)  Personal delivery; 
(2)  By letter addressed to the owner at the owner's address as recorded in the appraisal district records of Van Zandt County; or 
(3)  If personal service cannot be obtained, then by: 
a.  Publication in a newspaper of local circulation at least once; 
b.  By posting the notice on or near the front door of each building on the property to which the violation relates; or 
c.  By posting the notice on a placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates. 
(c)  Unless the condition described in the notice is corrected within ten days of such notice or of the publication, the penalty provided for in section 16-25 shall be applicable. Notice by mail shall be deemed complete when deposited in a post office or official depository of the United States Postal Service, with postage affixed and postage prepaid, addressed to the last known address of the owner. If the condition that violates this article continues, or resumes, more than ten days after notice, each day that it continues shall be a separate violation. If a condition that constitutes a violation is remedied after the required notice letter is sent (or notice published), but later returns or resumes within the same calendar year that the notice was sent or published, violation may be enforced without the requirement of an additional notice or publication. 
(d)  If the City mails a notice to a property owner in accordance with subsection (b), and the United States Postal Service returns the notice as "refused" or "unclaimed," the validity of the notice is not affected, and the notice is considered as delivered. 
(e)  In a notice provided under this section, the City may inform the owner by: 
(1)  Regular mail and a posting on the property; or 
(2)  By personally delivering the notice, that if the owner commits another violation of the same kind or nature that poses a danger to the public health and safety on or before the first anniversary of the date of the notice, the City without further notice may correct the violation at the owner's expense and assess the expense against the property. If a violation covered by a notice under this subsection occurs within the one-year period, and the City has not been informed in writing by the owner of an ownership change, then the City without further notice may take any action permitted under this article to correct or remedy the condition and assess its expenses as provided by Texas Health & Safety Code, § 342.007. 
(Code 1981, § 9.4; Ord. No. 05-05; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.4, 7-10-2007; Ord. No. 11-08, § 2, 12-13-2011) 
Sec. 16-23. - Correction or removal of conditions by city. 
(a)  The City may, after the ten days following the date of such notice of violation or of the publication, do such work as shall be reasonably necessary or cause such work to be done to bring such premises into compliance with the ordinances of the City. An administration fee as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the City Council from time to time plus labor costs and the cost of publication in newspaper shall be billed to the owner of the premises. 
(b)  Should such expense remain unpaid for a period of 30 days from the date of billing and has been rendered and furnished as per section 16-22, the City shall file with the county clerk a statement of expense incurred in correcting said violation. When such statement is filed, the City shall have a privileged lien on such property, second only to a tax lien. For any such expenditures, suit may be instituted and recovery and foreclosure had by the City. The statement of expense filed with the county clerk or certified copy thereof shall be prima facie proof of the amount expended and reasonableness of the charges. 
(Code 1981, § 9.5; Ord. No. 05-05; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.5, 7-10-2007; Ord. No. 11-08, § 2, 12-13-2011) 
Sec. 16-24. - Dead animals. 
    The lessee or owner of a dead animal (e.g., horse, cow, swine, dog, cat, etc.) located in the City or within 500 feet of the City limits shall dispose of the carcass within 24 hours of the death of the animal by either transporting the carcass to a rendering plant or burying it. 
(Code 1981, § 9.6; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.6, 7-10-2007) 
Sec. 16-25. - Failure to comply. 
    Any person who owns or occupies any property located within the City that is in violation of this article and who fails to comply, shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
(Code 1981, § 9.5; Ord. No. 05-05; Ord. No. 07-13, § 9.7, 7-10-2007; Ord. No. 11-08, § 2, 12-13-2011) 
Secs. 16-26-16-53. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ABANDONED AND JUNKED VEHICLES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 16-54. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Antique vehicle means a passenger car or truck that is at least 25 years old. 
    Motor vehicle means: 
(1)  Any motor driven or propelled vehicle required to be registered under the laws of this state; 
(2)  A trailer or semitrailer, other than manufactured housing, that has a gross vehicle weight that exceeds 4,000 pounds; 
(3)  A house trailer; 
(4)  An all-terrain vehicle, as defined by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 502.001, designed by the manufacturer for off-highway use that is not required to be registered under the laws of this state; or 
(5)  A motorcycle, motor-driven cycle, or moped that is not required to be registered under the laws of this state, other than a motorcycle, motor-driven cycle, or moped designed for and used exclusively on a golf course; and 
(6)  For purposes of this article, shall include a motorboat, outboard motor, or vessel subject to registration under V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 31. 
    Motor vehicle collector means a person who owns one or more antique or special interest vehicles and acquires, collects or disposes of an antique or special interest vehicle or part of an antique or special interest vehicle for personal use to restore and preserve an antique or special interest vehicle for historic interest. 
    Motor vehicle demolisher means a person in the business of: 
(1)  Converting motor vehicles into processed scrap or scrap metal; or 
(2)  Wrecking or dismantling motor vehicles. 
    Special interest vehicle means a motor vehicle of any age that has not been changed from original manufacturer's specifications and, because of its historic interests, is being preserved by a hobbyist. 
    Storage facility includes a garage, parking lot, or establishment for the servicing, repairing or parking of motor vehicles. 
    Vehicle means every mechanical device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a public way but excepting devices moved by human power or moved exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
(Code 1981, § 11.10; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-55. - Authorization to remove obstructing vehicle unaffected. 
    Nothing in this article shall affect a law authorizing the immediate removal of a vehicle left on public property that is an obstruction to traffic. 
(Code 1981, § 11.18; Ord. No. 01-01, § B) 
Secs. 16-56-16-83. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ABANDONED VEHICLES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Abandoned motor vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code ch. 683. 

Sec. 16-84. - Criteria for designation as abandoned. 
(a)  A motor vehicle is abandoned if the motor vehicle: 
(1)  Is inoperable, is more that five years old, and has been left unattended on public property for more than 48 hours; or 
(2)  Regardless of its age or condition: 
a.  Has remained illegally on public property for more than 48 hours; 
b.  Has remained on private property without the consent of the owner or person in charge of the property for more than 48 hours; or 
c.  Has been left unattended on the right-of-way of a designated county, state, or federal highway for more than 48 hours; 
(3)  Has been left unattended for more than 24 hours on the right-of-way of a turnpike project constructed and maintained by the Texas Turnpike Authority, division of the state department of transportation, or a controlled access highway; or 
(4)  Is considered an abandoned motor vehicle under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 644.153(r). 
(b)  In this section, "controlled access highway" has the meaning assigned by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 541.302. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(A); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-85. - Authority to take abandoned motor vehicle into custody. 
    The City Police Department may take into custody an abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor (hereinafter, "abandoned property") found on public or private property. Such agency may use its own personnel, equipment, and facilities or contract for other personnel, equipment, and facilities to remove, preserve, store, send notice regarding, and dispose of an abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor taken into custody by the agency. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(B); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-86. - Notification. 
    Should the police department take into custody any abandoned property as provided in section 16-85, it shall send notice of abandonment to: 
(1)  The last known registered owner of each motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor taken into custody by the agency or for which a report is received under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.031; and 
(2)  Each lienholder recorded under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code ch. 501 for the motor vehicle or, under V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 31, for the watercraft or outboard motor. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(C); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-87. - Contents of notice. 
    The notice provided for in section 16-86 must: 
(1)  Be sent by certified mail not later than the tenth day after the date the agency: 
a.  Takes the abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor into custody; or 
b.  Receives the report under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.031; 
(2)  Specify the year, make, model, and identification number of the item; 
(3)  Give the location of the facility where the item is being held; 
(4)  Inform the owner and lienholder of the right to claim the item not later than the 20th day after the date of the notice on payment of: 
a.  Towing, preservation, and storage charges; or 
b.  Garagekeeper's charges and fees under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.032 and, if the vehicle is a commercial motor vehicle impounded under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 644.153(q), the delinquent administrative penalty and costs; and 
(5)  State that failure of the owner or lienholder to claim the item during the period specified by subsection (4) of this section is: 
a.  A waiver by that person of all right, title, and interest in the item; and 
b.  Consent to the sale of the item at a public auction. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(D); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-88. - Publication of notice. 
    The notice provided for in section 16-86 may be given by publication in one newspaper of general circulation in the county if: 
(1)  The identity of the last registered owner cannot be determined; 
(2)  The registration has no address for the owner; or 
(3)  The determination with reasonable certainty of the identity and address of all lienholders is impossible. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(E); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-89. - Duration and content of published notice. 
    The notice of publication: 
(1)  Must be published in the same period that is required by section 16-87 for notice by certified mail and contain all of the information required by that section; and 
(2)  May contain a list of more than one abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(F); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-90. - Exemption from notice requirement. 
    The police department is not required to send a notice, as otherwise required by section 16-87, if the police department has received notice from a vehicle storage facility that an application has or will be submitted to the department for the disposal of the vehicle. 
Sec. 16-91. - Notification in case of theft and similar reports. 
    In addition to the notice required under section16-87, if the police department takes an abandoned motor vehicle into custody, the police department shall notify a person that files a theft report or similar report prepared by any law enforcement agency for the vehicle of that fact. The notice must be sent by regular mail on the next business day after the agency takes the vehicle into custody. The police department shall also provide the name and address of the person that filed the theft report or similar report to the vehicle storage facility or governmental vehicle storage facility that is storing the vehicle. 
Sec. 16-92. - Storage fees. 
    The police department or the agent of the police department that takes into custody an abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor is entitled to reasonable storage fees: 
(1)  For not more than ten days, beginning on the day the item is taken into custody and ending on the day the required notice is mailed; and 
(2)  Beginning on the day after the day the agency mails notice and ending on the day accrued charges are paid and the vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor is removed. 
Sec. 16-93. - Auction or use of abandoned items; waiver of rights. 
(a)  If an abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor is not claimed: 
(1)  The owner or lienholder: 
a.  Waives all rights and interests in the item; and 
b.  Consents to the sale of the item by public auction or the transfer of the item, if a watercraft, as provided by subsection (d) of this section; and 
(2)  The police department may sell the item at a public auction, transfer the item, if a watercraft, as provided by subsection (d) of this section, or use the item as provided by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.016. 
(b)  Proper notice of the auction shall be given. A garagekeeper who has a garagekeeper's lien shall be notified of the time and place of the auction. 
(c)  The purchaser of a motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor: 
(1)  Takes title free and clear of all liens and claims of ownership; 
(2)  Shall receive a sales receipt from the law enforcement agency; and 
(3)  Is entitled to register the motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor and receive a certificate of title. 
(d)  On consent of the state parks and wildlife department, the police department may transfer a watercraft that is not claimed to the state parks and wildlife department for use as part of an artificial reef under V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 89 or for other use by the state parks and wildlife department permitted under the Parks and Wildlife Code. On transfer of the watercraft, the state parks and wildlife department: 
(1)  Takes title free and clear of all liens and claims of ownership; and 
(2)  Is entitled to register the watercraft and receive a certificate of title. 
Sec. 16-94. - Auction proceeds. 
(a)  The police department is entitled to reimbursement from the proceeds of the sale of an abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft, or outboard motor for: 
(1)  The cost of the auction; 
(2)  Towing, preservation, and storage fees resulting from the taking into custody; and 
(3)  The cost of notice or publication as required by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.012. 
(b)  After deducting the reimbursement allowed under subsection (a) of this section, the proceeds of the sale shall be held for 90 days for the owner or lienholder of the vehicle. 
(c)  After the period provided by subsection (b) of this section, proceeds unclaimed by the owner or lienholder shall be deposited in an account that may be used for the payment of the auction, towing, preservation, storage, and notice and publication fees resulting from taking other vehicles, watercraft, or outboard motors into custody, if the proceeds from the sale of the other items are insufficient to meet those fees. 
(d)  The City may transfer funds in excess of $1,000.00 from the account to the City's general revenue account to be used by the police department. 
(e)  If the vehicle is a commercial motor vehicle impounded under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 644.153(q), the state department of public safety is entitled from the proceeds of the sale to an amount equal to the amount of the delinquent administrative penalty and costs. 
Sec. 16-95. - Use of certain abandoned motor vehicles. 
(a)  The police department that takes an abandoned motor vehicle into custody that is not claimed may: 
(1)  Use the vehicle for agency purposes; or 
(2)  Transfer the vehicle to any municipal or county agency or school district for the use of that agency or district. 
(b)  The police department shall auction the vehicle as provided by this article if the law enforcement agency or the City or county agency or school district to which the vehicle was transferred under subsection (a) of this section discontinues use of the vehicle. 
(c)  This section does not apply to an abandoned vehicle on which there is a garagekeeper's lien. 
(d)  The police department must comply with the notice requirements of V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.012 before the department may transfer a vehicle under subsection (a)(2) of this section. 
Sec. 16-96. - Authorization to remove obstructing vehicle unaffected. 
    Nothing in this division shall affect a law authorizing the immediate removal of a vehicle left on public property that is an obstruction to traffic. 
(Code 1981, § 11.11(H); Ord. No. 01-01) 
Secs. 16-97-16-120. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - JUNKED VEHICLES[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Junked vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.071 et seq. 

Sec. 16-121. - Defined. 
    In this division, "junked vehicle" means a vehicle that is self-propelled and: 
(1)  Displays an expired license plate or invalid motor vehicle inspection certificate or does not display a license plate or motor vehicle inspection certificate; and 
(2)  Is: 
a.  Wrecked, dismantled or partially dismantled, or discarded; or 
b.  Inoperable and has remained inoperable for more than: 
1.  Seventy-two consecutive hours, if the vehicle is on public property; or 
2.  Thirty consecutive days, if the vehicle is on private property. 
(Code 1980, § 1.12; Ord. No. 01-01; Ord. No. 11-05, § 2, 10-11-2011) 
Sec. 16-122. - Public nuisance. 
(a)  A junked vehicle, including a part of a junked vehicle, that is visible from a public place or public right-of-way is detrimental to the safety and welfare of the public, tends to reduce the value of private property, invites vandalism, creates a fire hazard, is an attractive nuisance creating a hazard to the health and safety of minors, produces urban blight adverse to the maintenance and continuing development of municipalities, and is a public nuisance. 
(b)  A person commits an offense if the person maintains a public nuisance. 
(c)  An offense under this section is subject to the penalties of section 1-12. 
(d)  Upon conviction of an offense under this section, the municipal court shall order abatement and removal of the nuisance. Removal shall be accomplished not later than the day following the date of such order. Beginning with the day following the date of such order, each day such nuisance continues unabated shall constitute a separate offense punishable at the new location. 
(Code 1981, § 11.13; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-123. - Authority to abate nuisance; procedures. 
    If an abatement of the nuisance and removal of the vehicle is sought to be accomplished, the following procedures, and those set forth in sections 16-124 and 16-125, shall be followed. 
(1)  Proper notice and public hearing is required before removal of the public nuisance. 
(2)  Once the notice is sent, the relocation of a junked vehicle to another location within the City limits shall have no effect upon the proceeding so commenced if the junked vehicle is deemed by the Chief of Police or the chief's designee to continue to constitute a public nuisance at the new location. 
(3)  After removal, a vehicle may not be reconstructed or made operable. 
(4)  No later than the fifth day after removal, a notice identifying the vehicle or part of the vehicle must be given to the state department of public safety. 
(5)  The municipal court of this City is designated as the hearing body to conduct under the procedures adopted under this article. Such court is directed to establish appropriate administrative procedures and may issue necessary orders to enforce the procedure so established, as well as those set forth in this article. 
(6)  All procedures for abatement and removal of a public nuisance must be administered by regularly salaried, full-time employees of this City; provided, however, that any authorized person may remove the nuisance. 
(7)  The Chief of Police, the chief's designee, and any other person authorized to administer these procedures may enter private property to examine a public nuisance, to obtain information to identify the nuisance, and to remove or direct the removal of the nuisance. 
(Code 1981, § 11.14; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-124. - Abatement and removal-Notice. 
(a)  If the Chief of Police or person designated by the chief determines that a nuisance as defined in section 16-122 exists, whether on public property, on a public right-of-way, or on private property, the chief (or such other person designated by the chief) shall issue a notice in writing stating the nature of the nuisance and that: 
(1)  The nuisance must be abated and removed not later than the tenth day after the date on which the notice was personally delivered or mailed; and 
(2)  Any request for a hearing must be made before that ten-day period expires. 
(b)  The City must provide not less than ten days' notice of the nature of the nuisance. The notice must be personally delivered, sent by certified mail with a five-day return requested, or delivered by the United States Postal Service with signature confirmation service to: 
(1)  The last known registered owner of the nuisance; 
(2)  Each lienholder of record of the nuisance; and 
(3)  The owner or occupant of the property on which the nuisance is located; or, if the nuisance is located on a public right-of-way, the property adjacent to the right-of-way. 
(c)  If the post office address of the last known registered owner of the nuisance is unknown, the notice may be placed on the nuisance or, if the owner is located, personally delivered. 
(d)  If a notice is returned undelivered, action to abate the nuisance shall be continued to a date not earlier than the 11th day after the date of the return. 
(e)  If no hearing has been requested within the time stipulated, citation for violation of this article shall be duly issued to appropriate persons, and enforcement hereof shall be accomplished by the same means as utilized in traffic offenses. 
(Code 1981, § 11.15; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-125. - Same-Hearing. 
(a)  If a hearing is requested by a person for whom notice is required, the hearing shall be held not earlier than the 11th day after the date of service of notice. 
(b)  At any such hearing, the junked vehicle is presumed, unless demonstrated otherwise by the owner, to be inoperable. 
(c)  At any such hearing, if the junked vehicle is found to be a public nuisance, the municipal court shall enter its order for abatement and removal as provided in section 16-122(d). Unless the nuisance has been abated and removed with the time stipulated in section 16-122(d), citation shall be duly issued to appropriate persons and enforcement hereof shall be accomplished by the same means as utilized in traffic offenses. 
(d)  If the information is available at the location of the nuisance, a resolution or order requiring removal of the nuisance must include the vehicle's: 
(1)  Description; 
(2)  Vehicle identification number; and 
(3)  License plate number. 
(Code 1981, § 11.16; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-126. - Disposal. 
(a)  After notice and, if requested, hearing, and upon entry of an order for abatement and removal, a junked vehicle, including a part of a junked vehicle, must be removed by the appropriate person. It may be removed by the City to a scrap yard, a motor vehicle demolisher, or other suitable site. 
(b)  The City may operate a disposal site if the City Council determines that commercial disposition of junked vehicles is not available or is inadequate. The City may: 
(1)  Finally dispose of a junked vehicle or vehicle part; or 
(2)  Transfer it to another disposal site if the disposal is scrap or salvage only. 
(Code 1981, § 11.17; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-127. - Exceptions. 
    Section 16-121 shall not apply to a vehicle or vehicle part: 
(1)  That is completely enclosed in a building in a lawful manner and is not visible from the street or other public or private property; or 
(2)  That is stored or parked in a lawful manner on private property in connection with the business of a licensed vehicle dealer or junkyard, or that is an antique or special interest vehicle stored by a motor vehicle collector on the collector's property, if the vehicle or part and the outdoor storage, if any, are: 
a.  Maintained in an orderly manner; 
b.  Not a health hazard; and 
c.  Screened from ordinary public view by appropriate means, including a fence, rapidly growing trees, or shrubbery. 
(Code 1981, § 11.18; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Sec. 16-128. - Governmental purpose. 
    All of the provisions provided in this article are hereby declared to be governmental and for the health, safety, and welfare of the citizens of this community and of the general public. Any member of the City Council or any duly appointed official or employee of this City charged with the enforcement of this article, acting for the City, in the discharge of duties, shall not thereby be rendered personally liable for, and is hereby relieved from all personal liability for any damages accruing or which may accrue to persons or property as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of such duties. 
(Code 1981, § 11.19; Ord. No. 01-01) 
Secs. 16-129-16-154. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - AUTO WRECKING AND SALVAGE OPERATIONS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- Automobile wrecking and salvage yards, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code ch. 396. 

Sec. 16-155. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Automobile graveyard means any location (whether operated as a business or otherwise) that is maintained, used, or operated for storing, keeping, buying, or selling junked, wrecked, scrapped, ruined, or dismantled motor vehicles (as the term "motor vehicle" is hereinafter defined) and motor vehicle parts. 
    Automotive wrecking and salvage yard means an outdoor place where a person stores three or more vehicles for the purpose of dismantling or wrecking the vehicles to remove parts for sale or for use in automotive repair or rebuilding. 
    Junk shall mean copper, brass, iron, steel, rope, rags, batteries, tires, or other material that has been discarded or sold at a nominal price by a previous owner of the material. The term does not include a wrecked vehicle. 
    Junked vehicle shall mean a vehicle that is self-propelled and: 
(1)  Does not have lawfully attached to it: 
a.  An unexpired license plate; and 
b.  A valid motor vehicle inspection certificate; and 
(2)  Is: 
a.  Wrecked, dismantled or partially dismantled, or discarded; or 
b.  Inoperable and has remained inoperable for more than: 
1.  72 consecutive hours, if the vehicle is on public property; or 
2.  30 consecutive days, if the vehicle is on private property. 
    Junkyard means a place where a business that owns junk, and is operated to store, buy, or sell junk, keeps all or part of the junk outdoors until the business disposes of the junk. 
    Motor vehicle means: 
(1)  Any motor driven or propelled vehicle required to be registered under the laws of this state; 
(2)  A trailer or semitrailer, other than manufactured housing, that has a gross vehicle weight that exceeds 4,000 pounds; 
(3)  A house trailer; 
(4)  An all-terrain vehicle, as defined by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 502.001, designed by the manufacturer for off-highway use that is not required to be registered under the laws of this state; or 
(5)  A motorcycle, motor-driven cycle, or moped that is not required to be registered under the laws of this state, other than a motorcycle, motor-driven cycle, or moped designed for and used exclusively on a golf course; and 
(6)  Includes a motorboat, outboard motor, or vessel subject to registration under V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 31: 
    Outdoor storage location means an outdoor location upon which or within which containers, discarded or unusable equipment, trash, rubbish, or other equipment is stored, kept or maintained in such manner as to be visible to the public. 
    Solid , as used in reference to a fence, wall, door or gate, means constructed and maintained so that the outer surface is continuous and without interstices, gaps, spaces, or holes; provided, however, that for the purposes of this article, a properly constructed and maintained chain link fence with strips or slats completely eliminating the ability to see through it is a solid fence. 
    Wrecked vehicle means a discarded, junked, damaged, or worn-out automotive vehicle that is not in a condition to be lawfully operated on a public road. 
    Yard means an automobile graveyard, an automobile wrecking and salvage yard and a junk yard, as the case may be. 
(Code 1981, § 11.21; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-156. - Purpose. 
    The City Council declares that to promote the health, safety, welfare, and convenience of its citizens as well as to promote tourism and business development within the City and to protect the public and private investment in physical improvements in this City, it is necessary to regulate the establishment, operation and maintenance of junkyards, automobile graveyards, and automobile wrecking and salvage yards. The City Council considers that the regulation of such operations, whether conducted for business purposes or otherwise, is a means of protecting and providing for the general welfare and promoting the safety of citizens of this City. The City Council further declares that, unless regulated, such operations are detrimental to the safety and welfare of the general public, tend to reduce the value of private and public property, invite vandalism, create fire hazards, constitute public and private nuisance creating hazards to the health and safety of citizens of this City and are detrimental to the economic welfare of the City and its citizens by producing urban blight adverse to the maintenance and continuing development of this City. 
(Code 1981, § 11.22; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-157. - License. 
    To protect the public health, safety, and welfare, any person who owns or intends to own and/or operate, whether for business purposes or otherwise, and automobile graveyard, and automobile wrecking and salvage yard or junkyard or an outdoor resale business or outdoor storage location within this City shall obtain from the City Secretary a non-assignable license authorizing such operation and shall renew the same annually in accordance with the terms and provisions of this section as set forth below: 
(1)  A fee as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the City Council from time to time is imposed for the issuance or renewal of a license. 
(2)  The validity of a license at any time is expressly conditioned upon the operation and maintenance of the yard or location in strict accordance with all of the terms and provisions of this article. Any such license may be suspended or revoked by the City for noncompliance with any requirement of this article. 
(3)  License renewals hereunder shall be effected annually not later than the first day of each fiscal year of this City. 
(4)  Fees received under this licensing program shall be deposited in the general fund of this City. 
(5)  No person who, on the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived, owns, operates or maintains an automotive graveyard, automotive wrecking and salvage yard or junkyard or an outdoor resale business or outdoor storage location within this City shall be required to obtain an original license covering such operation until the expiration of 90 days from such effective date. 
(Code 1981, § 11.23; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-158. - Screening requirements. 
(a)  Except as provided below in connection with the use of natural objects as a screen, any automobile graveyard, automobile wrecking and salvage yard or junkyard or outdoor storage location shall be completely surrounded and enclosed by a solid fence or wall. All sides of the yard shall be bounded by a solid fence or wall at least six feet in height. A fence or wall required by this article shall be constructed and maintained in compliance with the requirements set forth below: 
(1)  All fences shall be constructed of wood, masonry, corrugated sheet metal, chain link, or any combination, of those wall constructed of only one, as opposed to a combination, of those materials. 
(2)  Chainlink fences shall be constructed of galvanized chainlink fencing with wood or metal slats or strips run through all links of the chainlink fence. 
(3)  All fences or walls shall extend downward to within three inches of the ground and shall test plumb and square at all times. 
(4)  All fences or walls shall be constructed in compliance with all applicable provisions of any building code of this City as the same shall be effect at any time; provided, however, that should any provision of any such building code conflict, the more stringent requirement shall prevail. 
(b)  Any part of a fence or wall required by this article may consist in whole or in part of a solid wall and door, or walls and doors of any completely enclosed building on the premises, if that wall or door meets all construction requirements set forth in this article. 
(c)  In lieu of the solid fence requirement as set forth above, any location required by the terms and provisions of this article to be screened may be screened by natural objects such as plantings, hedges or trees; provided that any such natural object screen so used shall be at least as effective in completely screening any such location from public view as a fence meeting the requirements set forth above would have been had such a fence been constructed or any such location. 
(d)  Openings in the prescribed enclosure that are necessary to permit reasonable access to such yard shall be equipped with a solid gate or gates, constructed and maintained in accordance with the requirements for a fence or wall as set forth in subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1981, § 11.24; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-159. - Operating requirements of automobile graveyards, automobile wrecking and salvage yards, and junkyards. 
    The following regulations shall apply to all automobile graveyards, automobile wrecking and salvage yards, and all junkyards located with the City limits: 
(1)  Any license required and issued pursuant to this article shall be plainly displayed on this premises cover by the license. 
(2)  Any such yard shall be maintained in a sanitary condition and one which does not constitute a hazard to public health. 
(3)  No part of a yard not covered by any required license and/or which is not enclosed as set forth in section 16-158 shall be used as an automobile graveyard, an automobile wrecking and salvage yard or junkyard, and all operations thereon must be conducted within the required enclosure. 
(4)  Any such yard must have appropriate drainage and no water shall be allowed to stand in any place in or on the yard in such manner as to afford a breeding place for mosquitoes. 
(5)  Weeds and vegetation in or on the yard, other than flowers and trees, shall be kept at a height of not more than 12 inches. 
(6)  No garbage or other waste likely to emit foul or offensive odors or attract vermin shall be kept in or on the yard. 
(7)  No refuse of any kind (except salvageable parts) shall be kept or allowed to accumulate in or on the yard and any such salvageable parts shall be neatly stacked or segregated. 
(8)  No junk, parts or salvage shall be stored, allowed to rest upon or protrude, for any period of time whatever, over any public street, walkway or curb, and no refuse or trash shall be allowed to become scattered or blown away from or off the yard. 
(9)  Automobiles or other property shall not be stacked higher than one foot below the top of the required screening fence and, in order to provide firefighting accessibility, shall be kept and maintained at all times in rows not exceeding two automobiles in width, which rows shall be a minimum of ten feet apart. 
(10)  Neither motor vehicles nor junked vehicles, parts or other such property kept on or in the yard shall be allowed to deteriorate to the extent that such property becomes a health hazard or a fire hazard and, upon direction of appropriate health or fire inspectors, such property will be removed by the owner of the yard at the sole expense of such owner. 
(11)  All gasoline from any fuel tank, antifreeze fluid, motor oil or other liquids of an inoperable or junked vehicle, in or on the yard shall be completely drained and removed from such vehicle and no fluids or combustible material of any kind shall be allowed to remain in any inoperable or junked vehicle located in or on the yard. 
(12)  Inspection of a yard by designated representatives of the City will be permitted by the owner of the yard at any reasonable time. 
(13)  No such yard shall be allowed to become a nuisance, public or private, nor shall any such yard be operated or allowed to exist in such manner as to become injurious to the health, safety or welfare of the community or of any residents or businesses in the community. 
(14)  In connection with the operation or maintenance of such yard, no person shall. 
a.  Discharge or deposit upon any public or private property, including the yard, any industrial, chemical, hazardous, or other regulated waste, it being required hereby that all such materials be disposed of at a state-approved or federally approved disposal site; 
b.  Permit crankcase or radiator drainings, vehicle engine wash or other oils, greases, vehicle fuels, lubricants or like material to be discharged or deposited to any area of the City, including the yard; 
c.  Discharge into any sewage facility or creek bed any industrial or chemical waste which could have a bio-toxic effect upon such facility or upon any person or facility located downstream from such yard; 
d.  Cause any discharge of any material that constitutes a hazard to humans or wildlife; or 
e.  Allow junk, trash or other refuse to accumulate in any creek bed which would in any manner block or impede the flow of water. 
(15)  Any person who permits or commits a discharge prohibited by this section shall, in addition to any fine or penalty levied hereunder, be responsible for any cost or expense incurred by the City in the containment and/or mitigation of the prohibited discharge. 
(Code 1981, § 11.25; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-160. - Location of yard. 
    No fence required under the provisions of section 16-158 hereof for any automotive graveyard, automotive wrecking and salvage yard or junkyard may be located within 25 feet of the right-of-way of any public street or way; within 100 feet of a residence; or within 300 feet of a church or school; provided, however, that there shall be exempted from this location requirement any residence which is located adjacent to any such yard and which is owned or leased by the operator of any such yard; and further provided, that the distance requirements set forth herein shall not apply to any entity which is actively engaged in the business operation of any such yard as of the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
(Code 1981, § 11.26; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-161. - Public or private nuisance. 
    Any automobile graveyard, automobile wrecking and salvage yard or junkyard which is operated or maintained in violation or contravention of the screening requirements set forth in section 16-158 or in violation or contravention of the operating requirements set forth in section 16-159 shall be deemed to be and is hereby declared to be a public nuisance or a private nuisance, as the case may be. 
(Code 1981, § 11.27; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-162. - Enforcement. 
    Both civil and criminal remedies are provided herein for violation of any section of this article. 
(1)  Any person is entitled to appropriate injunctive relief to prevent a violation or threatened violation of this article from continuing or occurring. 
(2)  Any person who knowingly and intentionally violates this article is subject to the penalties of section 1-12. 
(Code 1981, § 11.28; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-163. - Cumulative effect. 
    This article shall be and is hereby declared to be cumulative of all other ordinances of this City and shall not operate to repeal or affect any other ordinance except insofar as the provisions thereof might be inconsistent or in conflict with the provisions of this article, in which event the more stringent provisions shall prevail. 
(Code 1981, § 11.29; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Sec. 16-164. - Governmental purpose. 
    All of the regulations provided in this article are hereby declared to be governmental and for the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of this community and of the general public. Any member of the City Council or any official or employee of this City charged with the enforcement of this article, acting for the City in the discharge of duties, shall not thereby be rendered personally liable, and is hereby relieved from all personal liability for any damage that might accrue to persons or property as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of such duties. 
(Code 1981, § 11.31; Ord. of 6-8-1992) 
Secs. 16-165-16-181. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - SMOKING IN CITY FACILITIES 

Sec. 16-182. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    City facility or facilities means all buildings, structures, and enclosed public areas owned or operated by or under the control of the City. 
    Smoke, smokes or smoking means carrying or holding a lighted pipe, cigar or cigarette of any kind or any other lighted smoking equipment or device; the combustion of any cigar, cigarette, tobacco or similar article; or any other combustible substance in any manner or in any form; and emitting or exhaling the smoke of a pipe, cigar, or cigarette of any kind. 
(Ord. No. 07-04, § 1, 5-15-2007) 
Sec. 16-183. - Smoking prohibited in City facilities; penalty. 
(a)  A person commits an offense if the person smokes in a City facility. 
(b)  Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties of section 1-12. A culpable mental state is not required for a violation of this article, and need not be proved. 
(Ord. No. 07-04, § 2, 5-15-2007) 
Sec. 16-184. - Signs. 
    Signs shall be visibly placed at or near a public entrance to City facilities to notify persons entering the premises that smoking is prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 07-04, § 3, 5-15-2007) 
Sec. 16-185. - Other applicable laws. 
    Nothing in this article excuses noncompliance with any state or federal law, provisions of this Code, any other applicable ordinance of the City, or any rule or regulation adopted pursuant thereto, which prohibits smoking. 
(Ord. No. 07-04, § 4, 5-15-2007) 
Secs. 16-186-16-208. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - DRILLING AND MINING[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
State Law reference- Oil and gas, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code ch. 81 et seq.; lease of municipal oil, gas or mineral land, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 253.005; disposition of the public domain, oil and gas, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code ch. 52; municipal regulation of exploration and development of mineral interests, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code § 92.007; access to property and records, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code § 91.1012. 

Sec. 16-209. - Permit required. 
    The City Council directs and establishes a permit required for any drilling for oil and/or gas and any mining for any natural material upon any City park and/or City-owned property. 
(Code 1981, § 18.70; Ord. No. 02-04) 
Secs. 16-210-16-229. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - NOISE CONTROL 

Sec. 16-230. - Noise interfering with enjoyment of property or public peace and comfort. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to make, cause to be made or allow any unreasonably loud, disturbing noise in the City, which is offensive to the ordinary sensibilities of inhabitants of the City, which noise renders the enjoyment of life or property uncomfortable or interferes with the public peace and comfort. 
(Ord. No. 10-02, § 2, 1-12-2010) 
Sec. 16-231. - Specific acts deemed loud and disturbing. 
    The following acts, among others, are declared to create loud and disturbing noises and shall be deemed a violation of this article, but such enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive: 
(1)  The sounding of any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, bus, streetcar or other vehicle, except as a danger signal, as required by state law. 
(2)  The playing, operating or permitting to be operated of any radio receiver set, phonograph, musical instrument, television, stereo or any other device in such a manner, or with such volume as to unreasonably disturb or interfere with the peace, quiet, comfort, or repose of persons of ordinary sensibilities, including neighboring persons, in any dwelling, apartment, hotel or other type of residence. 
(3)  The owning, keeping, possessing or harboring of any animal or fowl which, by frequent or habitual noise making, emits or makes an unreasonably loud, disturbing noise or interferes with the use, comfort and repose of neighboring persons of ordinary sensibilities. The provisions of this article shall apply to all public and private facilities, including any animal shelter, commercial kennel, or veterinary clinic, which hold or treat animals. 
(4)  The use of any automobile, motorcycle, streetcar, bus or vehicle so out of repair or so loaded, which emits or creates loud grating, grinding or rattling noise. 
(5)  The discharge into the open air of the exhaust from any motor vehicle except through a muffler or other device which will effectively and efficiently prevent loud and disturbing noises. 
(6)  The shouting and crying of peddlers, hawkers and vendors which disturbs the quiet and peace of the neighborhood. 
(7)  The use of any drum or other instrument or sound-amplifying equipment for the purpose of attracting attention by the creation of noise, to any performance, show, sale or display of merchandise as to attract customers to any place of business. 
(8)  The use of or permitting the use of mechanical loudspeakers or sound amplifiers in a fixed or moveable position mounted on any vehicle in or upon any street, alley, sidewalk, park, place or public property for the purpose of commercial advertising, giving instructions, directions, talks, addresses, lectures, or transmitting music to any person or persons or assemblages of persons in such a manner as to be offensive to the ordinary sensibilities of inhabitants of the City and so as to interfere with the public peace and comfort or make the enjoyment of life or property uncomfortable. 
(Ord. No. 10-02, § 2, 1-12-2010) 
Sec. 16-232. - Use of bell, siren, compression or exhaust whistle on vehicles. 
    No vehicle shall be equipped with and no person shall use upon a vehicle within the City any bell, siren, compression or exhaust whistle, except that vehicles operated in the performance of duty by law enforcement officers, fire department and ambulances may attach and use a bell, siren, compression or exhaust whistle. 
(Ord. No. 10-02, § 2, 1-12-2010) 
Sec. 16-233. - Exception for emergency, public service work, City-sponsored events or other permitted events. 
    Sound caused in the performance of emergency or public service work, including public utility operations, acting to protect the health, safety, or welfare of the community shall not be subject to the provisions of this article. Sound caused during City-sponsored events including, but not limited to, City parades, City festivals and any other City-sponsored events shall not be subject to the provisions of this article. Nothing in this paragraph, however, shall be construed to permit law enforcement, ambulance, fire or other City personnel to make excessive noise in the performance of their duties when such sound is clearly unnecessary. 
    Sound caused by the following activities or sources also shall not be subject to the provisions of this article: 
(1)  Railway locomotives and/or railway cars; 
(2)  Aircraft operations; 
(3)  Houses of worship bells or chimes; and 
(4)  Occasional outdoor gatherings, public dances, parades, shows, and/or sporting/ entertainment events provided that the events are conducted pursuant to a permit or license issued by the City relating to the staging of the events. 
    Nothing in this paragraph, however, shall be construed to permit the aforementioned activities or sources to make excessive noise in the performance of the activities, events or duties when such sound is clearly unnecessary. 
(Ord. No. 10-02, § 2, 1-12-2010) 
Sec. 16-234. - Enforcement responsibility. 
    The City police department shall have enforcement responsibility for the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 10-02, § 2, 1-12-2010) 
Sec. 16-235. - Penalties. 
    Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
(Ord. No. 10-02, § 2, 1-12-2010) 
Secs. 16-236-16-249. - Reserved. 
Chapter 18 - FIRE PROTECTION AND PREVENTION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal fire protection, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 342; safety, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 751 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 18-1. - Arson reward. 
    The City hereby offers a reward of $250.00 for the arrest and conviction of any person found guilty of committing the crime of arson within the corporate limits of said City. This reward is a standing offer, and shall be paid out of the general fund of the City. 
(Code 1981, § 7.70; Ord. of 12-3-1963) 
State Law reference- Arson generally, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 28.02; crime stoppers, V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 414. 
Secs. 18-2-18-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FIRE MARSHAL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Fire regulations, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 342; warrants for fire marshals, V.T.C.A., Code of Criminal Procedure art. 18.05. 

Sec. 18-21. - Creation of office. 
    The office of fire marshal is hereby created. Such office shall be independent of other City departments, the fire marshal reporting directly to the mayor and City Council. Such office shall be filled by appointment annually by the mayor, by and with the consent of the City Council. The said fire marshal shall be properly qualified for the duties of the office, and shall be removed only for cause. The fire marshal shall receive an annual salary as set by the City Council during budget preparation. 
(Code 1981, § 7.1; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-22. - Investigation of fires. 
    The fire marshal shall investigate the cause, origin and circumstances of every fire occurring within this City by which property has been destroyed or damaged, and shall especially make investigation as to whether such fire was the result of carelessness or design. Such investigation shall be begun within 24 hours, not including Sunday, of the occurrence of such fire. The fire marshal shall keep in the fire marshal's office a record of all fires, together with all facts, statistics and circumstances, including the origin of the fires and the amount of the loss, which may be determined by the investigation required by this article. 
(Code 1981, § 7.2; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-23. - Taking testimony. 
    The fire marshal, when of the opinion further investigation is necessary, shall take or cause to be taken the testimony, on oath, of all persons supposed to be cognizant of any facts or to have means of knowledge in relation to the matter under investigation, and shall cause the same to be reduced to writing; and if the fire marshal shall be of the opinion that there is evidence sufficient to charge any person with the crime of arson, or with the attempt to commit the crime of arson, or of conspiracy to defraud, or criminal conduct in connection with such fire, the fire marshal shall cause such person to be lawfully arrested and charged with such offense or either of them, and shall furnish to the proper prosecuting attorney all such evidence, together with the names of witnesses and all of the information obtained by the fire marshal, including a copy of all pertinent and material testimony taken in the case. 
(Code 1981, § 7.3; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-24. - Power to summon witnesses. 
    The fire marshal, after receiving the consent of a majority of the City Council, shall have the power to summon witnesses before the fire marshal to testify in relation to any matter which is by the provisions of this article a subject of inquiry and investigation, and may require the production of any book, paper or document or other piece of tangible evidence deemed pertinent thereto. The said fire marshal is hereby authorized and empowered to administer oaths and affirmations to any person appearing as witnesses before the fire marshal. 
(Code 1981, § 7.4; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-25. - Refusal to testify. 
(a)  Any witness who, after being summoned to appear and/or produce tangible evidence in the manner provided by section 18-24, refuses to be sworn, or who refuses to appear to testify, or who disobeys any lawful order of said fire marshal, or who fails or refuses to produce any book, paper or document or other piece of tangible evidence, touching any matter under examination, is guilty of a misdemeanor; and it shall be the duty of the fire marshal to cause all such offenders to be prosecuted. 
(b)  Any person violating this section is subject to the penalties in section 1-12; provided, however, that any person so convicted shall have the right of appeal. 
(Code 1981, § 7.5; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-26. - Private investigation requirement. 
    All investigations held by or under the direction of the fire marshal may, in the fire marshal's discretion or at the direction of the City Council, be private, and persons other than those required to be present may be excluded from the place where such investigation is held, and witnesses may be kept separate and apart from each other and not allowed to communicate with each other until they have been examined. 
(Code 1981, § 7.6; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-27. - Power to enter buildings. 
    The fire marshal shall have the authority at all times of day or night, when necessary, in the performance of the duties imposed upon the fire marshal by the provisions of this article, to enter upon and examine any building or premises where any fire has occurred, and other buildings and premises adjoining or near the same, which authority shall be exercised only with reason and good discretion. 
(Code 1981, § 7.7; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-28. - Monthly examinations. 
(a)  The fire marshal, upon complaint of any person having an interest in any building or property adjacent, and without any complaint, shall have a right at all reasonable hours, for the purpose of examination, to enter into and upon all buildings and premises within the City, and it shall be the fire marshal's duty, monthly or more often, to enter upon and make or cause to be entered and made, a thorough examination of all mercantile, manufacturing and public buildings, together with the premises belonging thereto. 
(b)  Whenever the fire marshal shall find any building or other structure which, for want of repair, or by reason of age or dilapidated condition, or for any cause, is especially liable to fire, and which is so situated as to endanger persons or property therein, and whenever the fire marshal shall find an improper or dangerous arrangements of stoves, ranges, furnaces or other heating appliances of any kind whatsoever, including without limitation chimneys, flues, and pipes with which the same may be connected, or a dangerous arrangement of lighting devices or systems, or a dangerous or unlawful storage of explosives, compounds, petroleum, gasoline, kerosene, dangerous chemicals, vegetable products, ashes, combustible, inflammable and refuse materials, or other conditions which may be dangerous in character or liable to cause or promote fire or create conditions dangerous to the firefighters or occupants, the fire marshal shall order the same to be removed or remedied, and such order shall be forthwith complied with by the aggrieved owner or occupant, the fire marshal may, within five days, appeal to the mayor, who shall investigate the cause of the complaint and unless by the mayor's authority the order is revoked, such order shall remain in force and be forthwith complied with by said owner or occupant. At the end of each month the fire marshal shall report to the state fire marshal all existing hazardous conditions, together with a separate report on each fire in the City during the month. 
(Code 1981, § 7.8; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-29. - Buildings liable to fire. 
    Any owner or occupant of a building or other structure or premises, who shall keep or maintain the same when, for want of repair, or by reason of age or dilapidated condition, or for any cause, it is especially liable to fire, and which is so situated as to endanger buildings or property of others, or is especially liable to fire and is so occupied that fire would endanger other persons or their property therein, shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
(Code 1981, § 7.9; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-30. - Improper arrangement of stoves and heating appliances. 
    The City prohibits the use of any and all dangerous chimneys, flues, fireplaces, stovepipes, ovens, and other apparatus (collectively, "apparatus") used in or about any building, other structure or premises and requires that the dangerous apparatus be removed or placed in a safe condition as required by the City's building codes and state law. It is a violation of this article when: 
(1)  Any owner or occupant of any building, other structure or premises who keeps or otherwise maintains any building, other structure or premises with an improper arrangement of a stove, range/oven, furnace or other heating appliance of any kind whatsoever, including but not limited to chimneys, flues, stovepipes, fireplaces, pipes and any other apparatus used in or about or otherwise connected to any building, other structure or premises so as to be dangerous due to fire hazard or the health and/or safety of persons or the property of others; 
(2)  Any owner or occupant of any building, other structure or premises who keeps or maintains any building, other structure or premises with an improper arrangement of a lighting device or system, or with the storage of explosives, petroleum, gasoline, kerosene, chemicals, vegetable products, ashes, combustibles, inflammable materials, refuse and/or any other condition that is dangerous due to fire hazard or the health and/or safety of persons or the property of others; or 
(3)  Any owner or occupant of any building, other structure or premises that creates a dangerous condition that promotes, augments, or causes fires, or that creates a dangerous condition for firefighters and/or occupants of such building, structure or premises. A violation of this article shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
(Code 1981, § 7.10; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Sec. 18-31. - Order before prosecution. 
    No prosecution shall be brought under sections 18-29 and 18-30 until the order provided for in section 18-28 is given, and the party notified shall fail or refuse to comply with the same. 
(Code 1981, § 7.11; Ord. of 7-11-1977) 
Secs. 18-32-18-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FIREWORKS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Authority of municipality to regulate the use of fireworks, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 342.003; regulation of fireworks and fireworks displays, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code ch. 2154. 

Sec. 18-51. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Fireworks means a composition or device: 
(1)  Designed for entertainment to produce a visible or audible effect by combustion, explosion, deflagration, or detonation; and 
(2)  Defined by 49 CFR 173.56(j)(1996). 
(Code 1981, § 9.10; Ord. of 8-14-1978) 
Sec. 18-52. - General requirements. 
    No person within the City limits may: 
(1)  Manufacture, sell, or give away fireworks; or 
(2)  Store, possesses, or uses fireworks, unless: 
a.  The fireworks are stored, possessed, or used for public display purposes and not for promotional or advertising purposes; and 
b.  The requirements of this article are satisfied. 
(Code 1981, § 9.11; Ord. of 8-14-1978) 
Sec. 18-53. - Permit requirement. 
    No person may store, possess, or use fireworks without first obtaining a permit for that purpose from the fire marshal. 
(Code 1981, § 9.12; Ord. of 8-14-1978) 
Sec. 18-54. - Application for permit. 
(a)  A permit applicant shall, at least ten days before using fireworks, file with the fire marshal a completed permit application showing the: 
(1)  Pyrotechnician's: 
a.  Business address; 
b.  Proof of legal competency; and 
c.  Record of previous experience with fireworks; 
(2)  Address of the proposed display; 
(3)  Amount, type, and class of fireworks to be used; 
(4)  Address of the company supplying the fireworks; 
(5)  Date of proposed display;
