Sec. 26-33. - Operational hours for City parks. 
    The City parks, playground, and recreational facilities owned or leased by the City shall be open for public use between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 12:00 midnight. Approved activities may exceed the 12:00 midnight closing time, for which prior approval must be obtained from the City Administrator or the City Administrator's designee. 
(Code 1981, § 18.55; Ord. No. 03-02) 
Sec. 26-34. - Athletic field inspections/closures in City parks and recreational areas. 
(a)  Reasons for athletic field closures. 
(1)  It is raining at game time. 
(2)  Baseball or softball infields are too wet. 
(3)  Athletic fields need to be closed in the interest of participant safety and/or preservation of good playing surfaces. 
(b)  Procedures for athletic field closures. 
(1)  Inspect athletic field by 4:00 p.m. 
(2)  Make a decision based upon field condition or weather. 
(3)  Consult with the appropriate athletic association's field manager, or designee, about the status of the field. 
(4)  Should the association's field manager and the City's representative not agree, the decision of the City representative shall take precedence. 
(5)  Continuously monitor weather and field conditions on evenings when fields will be in use after 6:00 p.m. When necessary a City representative will come in and close fields affected. 
(6)  The appropriate association's field manager has the responsibility to inform the association and the participants about field closures. 
(Code 1981, § 18.56; Ord. No. 03-02) 
Sec. 26-35. - All persons shall abide by all rules and requirements. 
(a)  Damage to park property. If any person damages or defaces any real or personal property in any recreational area or park owned or under the control or responsibility of the City, such person shall be held responsible for the actual costs to repair or replace such damaged item or items. 
(b)  The written rules and regulations concerning prohibited or regulated conduct shall be posted at conspicuous places in City parks and recreational areas. Proof that the person in charge of a supervised play or amusement activity verbally informed the actors that their conduct was disruptive to said supervised activity shall be prima facie evidence that the actors willfully disrupted, prevented or hindered such supervised play or amusement program and that such act constituted a nuisance. Any person accused of violating any rule or regulation may be expelled from all property and facilities of the City for such time as the City's designated representative shall direct. Any person expelled from a City park or recreational area of the City by the City's designated representative who comes upon any City park or City recreational area shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction may be subject to a fine. 
(Code 1981, § 18.57; Ord. No. 03-02; Ord. No. 12-06, § 3, 11-13-2012) 
Sec. 26-36. - Penalties. 
    Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
(Code 1981, § 18.58; Ord. No. 03-02) 
Chapter 28 - SECONDHAND GOODS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 28-1-28-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OCCASIONAL, YARD, OR GARAGE SALES 

Sec. 28-19. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Occasional sales means any sale of tangible personal property at retail, including, but not limited to, garage sales, patio sales, yard sales and all other on sites as herein provided by a person who does not hold themselves as to engage in or does not habitually engage in the business of selling such tangible personal property at retail. 
    Retail sales means all retail sales, except occasional sales, as that term is herein defined. 
(Code 1981, § 10.12; Ord. No. 05-03) 
Sec. 28-20. - Locations and conditions of conducting. 
    Occasional sales, including garage sales, patio sales, and yard sales, are hereby permitted within residential areas provided that: 
(1)  The number of such sales shall not exceed four during any calendar year; 
(2)  Such occasional sales are not conducted by any person or group of persons engaged in or who habitually engages in the business of selling such tangible property at retail; 
(3)  The sale shall be confined to the personal property to whom permit is obtained; 
(4)  No new merchandise (i.e., merchandise acquired solely for the purpose of resale) shall be sold at such occasional sale; 
(5)  The duration of each such sale shall not exceed three consecutive calendar days. 
(Code 1981, § 10.13; Ord. No. 05-03) 
Sec. 28-21. - Registration and fees. 
    Any individual desiring to conduct an occasional sale shall, a minimum of 24 hours prior to the sale, apply for a permit with the City Secretary, or the City Secretary's designee, by providing the name, address, date, and location of the proposed occasional sale. A permit fee shall be required as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the City Council from time to time. 
(Code 1981, § 10.14; Ord. No. 05-03) 
Sec. 28-22. - Penalty. 
    Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties in section 30-4(e). 
(Code 1981, § 10.16; Ord. No. 05-03) 
Chapter 30 - SIGNS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Regulation of signs by municipalities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 216. 

Sec. 30-1. - Purpose and intent. 
    The purpose of the regulations of this chapter is to encourage and promote a signage element of the City that is consistent with the high aesthetic standards established in other standards of the City's development. The regulations of this chapter are intended to be a positive tool to accomplish this purpose for the benefit of the general public, as well as the business community, and are not designed to discourage or inhibit aesthetically pleasing signage design, materials and placement. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.84), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-2. - Applicability. 
    The regulations of this chapter shall govern the placement and construction of all outdoor advertising display and signs within the City. In accordance with state law, the provisions of this chapter are extended into the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the City. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.85), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-3. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Awning means a structure hung from the surface of a building designed to provide protection from sun, rain, wind, and other climatological condition. An awning may be composed of fabric, steel, wood, Plexiglas, or other material. 
    Billboard means a large off-premises sign. 
    CBD means the central business district described in the City's zoning as the "B-3 District." 
    Election sign means a political sign relating to a particular election. 
    Flashing signs means all signs which alter their illuminated intensity through the use of a sequential-strobing light, rotating beacons, flashing lights, or other devices (including satellites) which cause the illumination to vary in intensity, brightness or display content. 
    Illuminated means any sign which has characters, letters, figures, designs, or outlines which are illuminated by electrical lights, luminous tubes, or other means which create light from an artificial source. 
    Logo means any formalized design, insignia, or trademark of a company or product which is commonly used to advertise that company or product. 
    Marquee means any "theater-type" sign in which letters are physically removable to allow for different messages. Marquee signs are generally illuminated. 
    Message sign means any sign which, through the use of independently illuminated light bulbs, displays the time, day, date, temperature, and brief messages, either in a scrolling, flashing, or digital manner. 
    Off-premises sign means a sign displaying advertising copy that pertains to a business, person, organization, activity, event, place, service, or product that is not principally located or primarily manufactured or sold on the premises on which the sign is located. 
    On-premises sign means a freestanding sign identifying or advertising a business, person, or activity, and installed and maintained on the same premises as the business, person or activity. 
    Pole sign means any sign which is freestanding from a structure or building and supported by, from, or on top of a pole or beam composed of metal, wood, plastic, or some other material. 
    Political sign means a sign relating to or dealing with the structure or affairs of government or politics, and includes signs relating to campaigns for elected office. 
    Portable sign means any outdoor advertising display which is movable from one location to another and which is not attached to a fixed structure or does not have supports embedded in the ground. The term "portable sign" shall specifically include an outdoor advertising display located in or on a vehicle, except where: 
(1)  Such sign merely identifies the vehicle as belonging to such business by displaying the name, address and/or telephone number of such business and/or identifying the type of product or service offered by such business; 
(2)  The primary use of such vehicle is for the transportation of persons or products or the delivery of services in connection with such business; and 
(3)  Such vehicle is currently state-licensed, state-inspected and in operable condition. 
A sandwich board sign or "A" frame sign is considered a portable sign. 
    Projecting sign means any sign that projects from a building at a 90-degree angle and which has one end attached to the building or other permanent structure. 
    Sign means an outdoor structure, sign, display, light device, figure, painting, drawing, message, plaque, poster, billboard, or other thing that is designed, intended, or used to advertise or inform. Any interior illuminated or moving sign, or light, which is visible from the exterior of a structure may be determined as being erected on the exterior of the building or structure. 
    Window sign means any sign, banner, or painted message which is displayed from the building interior and is visible through the window of the establishment. This type of sign is one that is intended directly for viewing from the outside and does not include interior signs which may be partially visible from the outside of the establishment. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.86), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-4. - Off-premises, temporary and other short-term signs. 
(a)  Prohibited signs. Except as provided in subsections (b) and (c) of this section, all off-premises signs are prohibited and no permit shall be granted for the construction of any off-premises signs. 
(b)  Temporary signs. Signs that are removed in their entirety (including both display features and the structures to which the display features are attached) no later than 20 days after the sign is first put in place are excepted from this chapter, so long as any such signs are only displayed for no more than 40 days per calendar year for any one particular business, person, organization, activity, event, place, service, or product. 
(c)  Election signs. Election signs may only be displayed for a period beginning on the date of the filing deadline for the particular election to which the election sign is related and ending no more than seven days after the election. 
(d)  Political signs. No political signs shall be located on any property owned by the City. 
(e)  Occasional sales signs. Two off-premises signs shall be permitted, not to exceed two square feet in size, related to occasional sales as defined in chapter 28. No off-premises signs shall be permitted on utility poles or on public rights-of-way. Signs posted under this subsection may be posted a maximum of two days prior to the beginning date of the occasional sale and shall be removed within 24 hours following the last date of the occasional sale. Notwithstanding any other ordinance provision to the contrary, the failure to obtain an occasional sale permit prior to the beginning date of the occasional sale shall result in an increase of the permit fee to $25.00, and the failure to timely remove all off-premises signs allowed under this subsection shall result in a penalty not to exceed $25.00 per sign. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.87), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-5. - Signs located in the Central Business District (B-3). 
    The following standards shall apply to all property located within the area zoned CBD (B-3). The term "property" shall include, but is not limited to, commercial, office, retail, residential, industrial, municipal, and institutional premises. 
(1)  Permitted signs. Only three classes of signs (other than traffic control signs) will be permitted in the CBD (B-3): 
a.  Wall signs. 
1.  Intent. This type of sign shall be favored within the CBD (B-3). It may be mounted with an awning on the same building facade. The standards in this subsection also apply to signs painted directly on the building surface. 
2.  Minimum height. No wall sign may be mounted in a manner that results in the lowest portion of the sign being less than 61/2 feet or greater than 20 feet above the sidewalk surface. Businesses and offices may mount signs at lower elevations that indicate the name of the establishment and street address only. These signs must not exceed eight square feet. 
3.  Maximum height. Wall signs shall be allowed a maximum height of 20 feet at their highest point above the sidewalk surface. They shall not be allowed to extend above the existing building roof line. Where a building is less than 20 feet tall, the roof line shall constitute the maximum allowable elevation. 
4.  Thickness. Wall signs do not have to be flush with the building surface. To accommodate structural and electrical equipment, a wall sign may be up to one foot thick. 
5.  Area. There shall be only one display face for a wall sign. Allowable footage shall be based on the following table: 
Building 
Frontage Surface Area 
(One-Story) Additional Area 
(Per Story) Max. 
Area 1-50 linear feet 25 sq. ft. 55 sq. ft. 40 sq. ft. 51-100 linear feet 30 sq. ft. 55 sq. ft. 45 sq. ft. Over 100 linear feet 35 sq. ft. 10 sq. ft. 50 sq. ft.  
6.  Illumination. Wall signs may be illuminated internally through the use of fluorescent tubes. These may also be externally illuminated through the use of "gooseneck" reflectors and lights, provided that such reflectors are equipped with proper glass lenses concentrating the illumination upon the surface of the sign so as to prevent glare upon the street or adjacent property. Spotlights and floodlights may also be used to externally illuminate wall signs provided that the lights are so directed or shielded that the light source is not directly visible from any street, sidewalk, or adjacent property. 
7.  Movement. Wall signs shall not be permitted to move, rotate, gyrate, or give the impression of movement. 
8.  Lettering. Wall signs may have lettering up to 31/2 feet in height. Letters should be contained within the sign face. Individually mounted letters must be no greater than four feet in height. Letters must be permanent and nonremovable. 
9.  Number. There shall be only one wall sign per business or each building facade. The total area of all signs per facade must not exceed the area standard set forth above for the cumulative sum of all signs. 
b.  Marquee signs. 
1.  Intent. Marquee signs are to be generally considered as "theater-type" signs, which have changeable message boards. Use of a marquee sign will be limited to entertainment-oriented land uses (movie theaters, dramatic theaters, civic centers, opera houses, restaurants, etc.). Verification of this fact will be required on the sign permit. 
2.  Minimum height. The lowest portion of a marquee sign must be no less than eight feet or no greater than 20 feet above the sidewalk surface, or integrated into existing pole signs. 
3.  Maximum height. Marquee signs shall be no greater than 20 feet above the sidewalk surface at their highest point. Marquee signs shall not extend more than five feet above the existing building roof line. Where a building is less than 20 feet tall, the roof line shall constitute the maximum allowable elevation. 
4.  Projection. Marquee signs shall be no greater than six feet from the building surface. A distance of at least two feet shall be maintained between the outer edge of the marquee sign and any traffic control sign. 
5.  Movement. Marquee signs shall not be permitted to move, rotate, gyrate, or give the impression of movement. 
6.  Number. One marquee sign per business shall be allowed. 
7.  Separation. All marquee signs shall be no closer than 30 feet from neighboring signs, measured by the nearest face to the nearest face. 
c.  Projecting signs. 
1.  Minimum and maximum heights. The lowest portion of a projecting sign must be no less than 71/2 feet or no greater than 12 feet above the sidewalk surface. 
2.  Area. Maximum four square feet per sign one-sided or two-sided. 
3.  Projection. Projecting signs shall be no greater than two feet from the building surface. A distance of at least two feet shall be maintained between the outer edge of the projecting sign and any traffic control sign. 
4.  Movement. Projection signs shall not be permitted to move, rotate, gyrate, or give the impression of movement. 
5.  Number. One projecting sign per building shall be allowed. 
6.  Separation. All projecting signs shall be no closer than 20 feet from neighboring signs, measured by the nearest face to the nearest face. 
(2)  Prohibitions. The following types of signs (both interior and exterior) shall not be permitted within the CBD: off-premises, portable, pole (except by special exception), vehicular, banner (except by special exception), bench, roof, flashing, and any other type of sign which does not come under the three classifications provided in this section. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.88), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-6. - On-premises/off-premises signs located on property outside the central business district and on property in the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the City. 
    The following standards shall apply to all property within the City limits and in the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the City, but outside the CBD. The term "property" shall include, but is not limited to, commercial, office, retail, residential, industrial, municipal, and institutional premises. 
(1)  Billboard and off-premises sign prohibition. Billboards and off-premises signs are prohibited in all areas inside the City limits and areas within the City's extraterritorial jurisdiction. 
(2)  Freestanding on-premises sign requirements. 
a.  Maximum area. 300 square feet per face. Temporary extensions, or cutouts, shall not exceed 20 percent of the sign area. 
b.  Minimum setback. Five feet outside the existing right-of-way. 
c.  Maximum height. 30 feet. 
d.  Spacing, off-premises. No off-premises sign shall be within 4,500 feet along the right-of-way of another off-premises sign. 
e.  Placement. No sign of this classification may be located within 75 feet of any residential area that is along the same right-of-way of the proposed sign. 
f.  Construction. Signs may not be attached to a building, and must only be of a monopole, steel nature. 
g.  Illumination. Signs may be illuminated internally through the use of fluorescent tubes or externally through the use of gooseneck reflectors and light, provided that such reflectors are provided with proper glass lenses concentrating the illumination upon the area of the sign so as to prevent glare upon the street or adjacent property. No flashing intermittent lights shall be allowed, and no lights may interfere with any traffic signal. 
(3)  On-premises sign requirements for signs attached to a building/structure. 
a.  Maximum area. There shall be only two display faces for on-premises signs. Allowable footage shall be based on the following table: 
Building Frontage Surface Area Maximum Height Ground 
Clearance 1-50 linear feet 60 sq. ft. 18 ft. 8 ft. 51-100 linear feet 100 sq. ft. 20 ft. 8 ft. 101-150 linear feet 150 sq. ft. 25 ft. 12 ft. Over 150 linear feet 200 sq. ft. 30 ft. 15 ft.  
b.  Minimum setback. Five feet outside the existing right-of-way. 
c.  Spacing, on-premises. No more than one on-premises sign per platted lot. 
d.  Placement. No sign of this classification may be located within 50 feet of any residential area. 
e.  Construction. Signs may be attached to building. Any sign not attached to the building must only be of a monopole or bi-pole, steel or wood nature. 
f.  Design. All signs shall be designed and constructed to wind pressures as outlined in the building code adopted by the City. 
g.  llumination. Signs may be illuminated internally through the use of fluorescent tubes, or externally through the use of gooseneck reflectors and light, provided that such reflectors are provided with proper glass lenses concentrating the illumination upon the area of the sign so as to prevent glare upon the street or adjacent property. No flashing intermittent lights shall be allowed, and no lights may interfere with any traffic signal. 
h.  Movement. Signs permitted under this section shall not be permitted to move, rotate, or gyrate by electrical or mechanical means or give the impression of movement through the use of diffraction grates or wind-sensitive/light sensitive surfaces. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.89), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-7. - Exceptions. 
    The following signs are not regulated by the foregoing standards, shall not be required to obtain a permit under this chapter, and are otherwise governed by the following provisions: 
(1)  Traffic control signs. Any sign installed and maintained by the City, by the county, or by any department of the state which is in conformance with the Texas Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices. 
(2)  City signs. Any sign or banner installed and maintained by the City. 
(3)  Construction signs. Any construction sign (one per lot) not exceeding 40 square feet in area which indicates the owner, architect, financial institution, and/or general contractor. 
(4)  Information signs. Warning signs, security signs, parking direction signs, and community or school information signs or banners. 
(5)  Real estate signs. Any non-illuminated temporary real estate sign of eight square feet or less which announces availability of real property through sale or lease. One real estate sign per building or lot is allowed. 
(6)  Political signs. Any sign pertaining to a public election which is located on private real property with the consent of the property owner that has an effective area 36 square feet or less, is eight feet high or less, is not illuminated, and does not have any moving elements. 
(7)  Message signs. Approved bank or financial institution message signs which scroll or flash the time, date, temperature, and a brief message. The message cannot change faster than once every five seconds. No physical movement will be permitted. These signs must not encroach on the City or state right-of-way. 
(8)  On-site banners. A banner may be used as a temporary on-premises sign for up 30 days. Banners will be hung from the wall only, and are subject to all pertinent standards and permit procedures. Streamers and promotional flags are not allowed. A maximum of one banner per business shall be allowed. 
(9)  Off-site special event banners. A temporary banner promoting a public event may be erected subject to the following special permitting procedures: 
a.  Application for a temporary permit must be submitted in writing to the code compliance officer 30 days prior to the opening date of the event. The application shall include the name of the organization making the request, a contact name and information, the dates, times and location of the event, the nature of the event, the size of the banner, the proposed location of the sign or banner, and signed permission from the property owner of the proposed banner site. 
b.  The code compliance officer shall review the application and make a determination based on the established criteria within five business days. Criteria for approval shall include: 
1.  The event must be sponsored by an area nonprofit or civic organization or a local chapter of a nonprofit organization, or benefit a local charity or charitable organization; 
2.  The event must be open to the public; 
3.  The event must be held in the Wills Point area; and 
4.  The banner or sign must not impede the visibility of vehicular traffic. 
c.  A temporary permit is valid for a maximum of 25 days prior to the opening date of the event and must be removed within two business days after the close of the event. The effective days and duration of the permit shall be set by the code compliance officer and shall be displayed on the permit. 
(10)  Interior signs. Any interior sign which is not visible from the centerline of the street parallel with the building facade shall be allowed. 
(11)  Flags. Any business may display a governmental flag in an appropriate, respectful manner. 
(12)  Historical markers. Any sign or plaque designating a local, state, or national landmark. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.90), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-8. - General provisions. 
(a)  Content. The City does not regulate the content of signs; however, no sign shall contain any obscene, indecent or immoral words, pictures, descriptions or other such matter. 
(b)  Out-of-compliance signs. All signs within the City shall be maintained as to copy quality, structural neatness, and ground foliage. Failure to comply can result in permit revocation and removal of said structure at owner's expense. 
(c)  Electrical. Prior to the issuance of any permit for signs with lighting, a licensed electrician shall apply for an electrical permit and the local power company engineer shall verify that there is a minimum ten-foot clearance between any portion of the sign and all overhead power lines. 
(d)  Location. Signs permitted pursuant to this chapter may be located only in districts zoned B-1, B-2, B-3, and I, and must be situated no less than 100 feet from any residential or agricultural zoning district. 
(e)  Rights-of-way. No sign may be constructed or posted on a public or railroad right-of-way, and any sign constructed near such areas shall have a setback of no less than five feet from such rights-of-way. No sign shall be placed on a utility or traffic control pole, except when clearly permitted by state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.91), 7-8-2008; Ord. No. 17-11, § 2, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 30-9. - Nonconforming signs. 
(a)  All existing signs and awnings permanently affixed to a structure or real estate within the City limits on the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived shall be allowed to operate as nonconforming signs, if such signs and awnings were not erected in violation of the ordinances in effect at the time of their erection. In the event that a sign or awning permitted to remain in place as a nonconforming sign is blown down, or otherwise destroyed, or dismantled for any purpose other than maintenance operations or for changing letters, symbols, or other matter on such sign or awning, said sign may not be reconstructed or repaired except to conform to the provisions of this chapter. A sign or awning is considered to have been destroyed if the cost of repairing the sign or awning is more than 60 percent of the cost of erecting a new sign or awning of the same type at the same location. No sign presently in a public or railroad right-of-way shall be allowed to operate as a nonconforming sign under the provisions of this section. 
(b)  No person may cause an increase in the extent of nonconformity of a nonconforming sign. Illumination may not be added to a nonconforming sign. 
(c)  A nonconforming sign may not be moved or replaced except to bring the sign into conformity with this chapter. 
(d)  If a nonconforming sign remains blank for a continuous period of 180 days, that sign shall be deemed abandoned and shall, within 90 days after such abandonment, be altered to comply with the sign regulations in this chapter or be removed by the sign owner, owner of the property where the sign is located, or other person having control over such a sign. For purposes of this section, a sign is "blank" if: 
(1)  It advertises a business, service, commodity, accommodation, attraction or other enterprise or activity that is no longer operating or being offered or conducted; 
(2)  The advertising message it displays becomes illegible in whole or substantial part; or 
(3)  The advertising copy paid for by a party other than the sign owner or promoting an interest other than the rental of the sign has been removed. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.92), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-10. - Removing obsolete signs. 
(a)  All signs relating to a product no longer available for purchase by the public and all signs relating to a business which has been closed for at least six months or has moved away shall be termed obsolete. All advertising copy shall be removed, and painted wall signs shall be painted over with a color that resembles or matches the wall. If the owner or person responsible for the sign or if the tenant closing the business fails to remove or paint over the sign, the owner of the premises shall be responsible, and the work shall be done within 30 days following the date of obsolescence. All off-premises signs must be removed within 60 days following the date of obsolescence, or provide evidence that the sign will be used within 60 days. Said off-premises signs may be donated to the City. 
(b)  Notice to alter or remove signs. 
(1)  Any sign which is found to be in violation of this chapter may be removed by the code compliance officer after notification is given as provided herein. The notice shall: 
a.  Be personally delivered or sent by certified mail, return receipt requested to the owner of the property or of the sign; 
b.  Describe the nature of the violation; 
c.  Order the correction of the violation within a specified time, which shall not be less than five business days from the receipt of the notice; and 
d.  Give notice that the code compliance officer may remove and impound the unlawful sign at the owner's expense if the violation is not corrected within the time specified in the notice. 
(2)  If the person or business ordered to correct the violation fails to do so within the time specified, the code compliance officer may remove or cause removal of the unlawful sign; provided, however, that the person aggrieved by said notice or order may file an appeal with the board of adjustment in accordance with the provisions applicable for other appeals if timely filed. The procedures applicable to other appeals shall be followed and the order of the code compliance officer shall be stayed in accordance thereof, pending the final determination of the board of adjustment. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.93), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-11. - Permits. 
(a)  No sign, banner, or awning shall be erected within the City limits after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived unless the owner or lessee of the premises on which such sign, banner or awning is to be erected first obtains a permit from the code compliance officer. Signs to be erected in the CBD must be reviewed and approved by the City Planning Commission prior to receiving a permit. 
(b)  In order to obtain a building permit, a detailed drawing of the sign, awning, or banner must be submitted to the code compliance officer for approval, and the site of the sign must be flagged or marked. The filing fee will be based on the estimated cost of construction at the same rate established for building permits. 
(c)  The applicant must acquire all necessary building permits, as they apply to the particular sign, banner, or awning. All construction work is subject to City code enforcement. 
(d)  Any applicable state permit must be obtained prior to applying for a permit from the City. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.94), 7-8-2008) 
Sec. 30-12. - Enforcement. 
    All new signs, banners, and awnings constructed, erected, hung or displayed within the City and its extraterritorial jurisdiction after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived must comply with the regulations set forth in this chapter. The code compliance officer shall be responsible for enforcement of the provisions of this chapter. Any person violating this chapter shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
(Ord. No. 08-08, § 2(6.95), 7-8-2008) 
Chapter 32 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Minimum standards of sanitation and health protection measures, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 341; local regulation of sanitation, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 342; Solid Waste Disposal Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 361; municipal solid waste, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 363; litter, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 365. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 32-1-32-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DUMPING AND BURNING 

Sec. 32-19. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Combustible material means and includes all rubber of any kind, tires, plastics, carpets, treated lumber and similar refuse. 
    Garbage means and includes all animal and vegetable matter, waste material and refuse from kitchens, residences, and other premises, and shall include any and all toxic substances. 
    Rubbish means and includes all waste materials of any kind, such as scrap building materials, scrap metal, old automobile frames and parts, and any and all other substances which have been abandoned and are not neatly maintained for future use or sale. 
    Trash means and includes all waste paper, rags, boxes, grass, shrubs, yard and house cleanings, grass clippings, leaves, tree trimmings, glass, tin cans, ashes and similar refuse. 
(Code 1981, § 8.10; Ord. No. 08-04, § 8.10, 4-8-2008) 
Sec. 32-20. - Purpose. 
(a)  This article is adopted to prohibit the presence in the atmosphere of one or more air contaminants or combinations thereof in such concentration and of such duration as may tend to be injurious to or otherwise adversely affect human health or welfare, animal life, vegetation or property, or as to interfere with the normal use and enjoyment of animal life, vegetation or property. 
(b)  This article also is intended to prohibit the burning of rubbish, garbage, combustible materials and/or trash of any kind within the City limits. 
(Code 1981, § 8.11; Ord. No. 08-04, § 8.11, 4-8-2008) 
Sec. 32-21. - Burning and dumping prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, corporation and/or organization to burn, dump and/or deposit any rubbish, garbage, combustible material, trash and/or other refuse in or upon any street or alley, whether public or private, within the City limits. 
(Code 1981, § 8.12; Ord. No. 08-04, § 8.12, 4-8-2008) 
Sec. 32-22. - Burning prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, to burn any rubbish, garbage, combustible material and/or trash of any kind, as defined in section 32-19, within the City limits at any time and under any circumstances. The burning, within the City limits, of any rubbish, garbage, combustible material, trash and/or any other substance that shall be particularly obnoxious due to smoke or odor, or the burning of which may endanger the public health, safety or welfare, including but not limited to, damage to property or vegetation and/or creation of a toxic or hazardous condition, shall be considered a nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 08-04, § 8.13, 4-8-2008) 
Sec. 32-23. - Penalty. 
    Any person convicted of violating this article shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. Each day an offense occurs is a separate violation. 
(Ord. No. 08-04, § 8.14, 4-8-2008) 
Sec. 32-24. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 12-01, § 2, adopted Feb. 12, 2012 , repealed § 32-24, which pertained to the burn ban variance municipal review board. See Code Comparative Table for complete derivation. 
Sec. 32-25. - Variances. 
(a)  A variance to the provisions of this burn ban regulation shall be considered an exception to the City's burn regulations, rather than a right. The City Administrator may authorize a variance from the regulations of this burn ban regulation when, in the City Administrator's opinion, undue hardship will result from requiring strict compliance with this regulation. The following limitations and criteria shall be used by the City Administrator to evaluate, grant or deny any burn ban variance request: 
(1)  Undue hardship. Special circumstances exist which affect the land and development involved such that the strict application of the provisions of this burn ban regulation: 
a.  Would deprive the owner or applicant of the ability to use the land appropriately, such as to construct new structures and/or buildings on the land and/or clean-up/beautify the land, which would promote public health and safety; 
b.  Granting of a variance shall be based upon a finding that the applicant's difficulties or hardship is due to unusual conditions or circumstances, such as a large amount of trash debris as defined in section 32-19; 
c.  Granting of a variance will not adversely affect surrounding property owners and their use; 
d.  Granting a variance shall not be detrimental to public health, safety and/or welfare; and 
e.  Financial hardship alone shall not be grounds for a variance. 
(2)  A variance shall not be approved if the circumstance for the hardship is caused or created by the owner of the property or the applicant seeking the variance. 
(b)  The applicant shall be responsible for providing all the data, documentation and/or justification for the requested variance. 
(c)  If the City Administrator deems it necessary and/or upon the applicant's request, the City shall hold a public hearing within 30 days after the completed application for a variance is filed and the fees paid. Ten days before the public hearing, a notice of a public hearing shall be sent via regular U.S. mail to all property owners within 200 feet of the affected property. Notice of the public hearing shall also be published in the official local newspaper ten days before the public hearing. 
(d)  If the City Administrator determines that a variance shall not be granted, then the applicant has the right to appeal the City Administrator's decision to the City Council for review at the next regularly-scheduled City Council meeting. All appeals must be made within ten days of the City Administrator's final decision. The City Council's decision is final. 
(e)  An application for a variance shall be made in writing in a form prescribed by the City and shall be accompanied by a fee, a burn site plan, mailing labels for property owner notification and any other information necessary to illustrate the reason for the variance request. 
(f)  The City Administrator may impose such conditions, limitations, safeguards, instructions and/or time restrictions that he or she deems necessary to the granting of any variance. Violation of any condition, limitation, safeguard, instruction or other restriction shall constitute a violation of this regulation. The following guidelines shall be followed as minimum requirements to burning: 
(1)  Burning shall be commenced and conducted only when wind direction and other meteorological conditions are such that smoke and other pollutants will not cause adverse effects to any public road, landing strip, navigable water, or off-site structure containing sensitive receptors. 
(2)  If at any time the burning causes or may tend to cause smoke to blow onto or across a road or highway, it shall be the responsibility of the applicant and/or other person initiating the burn to have flag persons posted on the affected road or highway to notify drivers, residents, and all other affected persons of this condition. 
(3)  Burning must be conducted downwind of, or at least 500 feet from any structure containing sensitive receptors located on adjacent properties unless prior written approval is obtained from the adjacent property owners and/or occupants with possessory control over said property. 
(4)  Burning shall be conducted in compliance with the following meteorological and timing considerations: 
a.  The initiation of burning shall commence no earlier than one hour after sunrise. Burning shall be completed on the same day and not later than one hour before sunset, and shall be attended by a responsible person at all times during the active burn phase when the fire is progressing. In cases where residual fires and/or smoldering objects continue to emit smoke after this time, such areas shall be extinguished if the smoke from these areas has the potential to create a nuisance or traffic hazard condition. In no case shall the extent of the burn area be allowed to increase after these stated times. 
b.  Burning shall not be commenced when the surface wind speed is predicted to be less than six miles per hour (five knots) or greater than 23 miles per hour (20 knots) during the burn period. 
c.  Burning shall not be conducted during periods of actual or predicted persistent low-level atmospheric temperature inversions. 
(g)  In addition to any other fees imposed by the City (including but not limited to an application fee), the City shall charge a fee as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the City Council from time to time for a fire apparatus/truck and Wills Point Volunteer Fire Department personnel to be available during the time of the controlled fire/burn. There shall be a minimum charge of one hour. Additional charges may apply, as needed. This minimum charge shall be due and must be paid at the time of scheduling the controlled fire/burn with the Wills Point Volunteer Fire Department. 
(h)  The following materials shall not be burned under any circumstances, which includes, but is not limited to: electrical insulation, treated lumber, plastics, non-wood construction/demolition materials, heavy oils, asphalt materials, potentially explosive materials, chemical wastes, and/or materials containing natural and/or synthetic rubber. 
(i)  If after the fire/burning commences, complaints are received about the level of smoke and/or other contaminants originating from the controlled fire/burning, the complaints will be forwarded immediately to the person overseeing the controlled burn and all burning shall cease and be extinguished immediately. If the person overseeing the controlled burn deems it necessary it shall be extinguished immediately, it shall be the applicant's (or designee's) responsibility to make other, alternate arrangements to remove the trash debris from the affected property in an appropriate manner. 
(j)  All trash debris that is authorized to be burned in the variance, must originate on the affected property. At no time shall any debris of any kind be brought in from another location, deposited, or otherwise discarded on the subject property to be burned. 
(k)  After the City Administrator approves a burn variance, it is the applicant's (or designee's) responsibility to contact the Wills Point Volunteer Fire Department to schedule a date and time to commence such burning. The Fire Chief, or the Fire Chief's designee, has the sole discretion to decide the date and time such authorized burning shall commence. Any variance granted by the City Administrator that is not exercised within 90 days from the date of granting shall lapse and may only be reinstated after a new application is submitted along with the fees and all other requisites are met in accordance with this article and state law. 
(Ord. No. 08-05, § 8.15(B), 6-10-2008; Ord. No. 12-01, § 3, 2-12-2012 ) 
Sec. 32-26. - Other applicable laws. 
    Nothing in this article excuses noncompliance with any state or federal law, provisions of this article, any other applicable ordinance of the City, or any rule or regulation adopted pursuant thereto, which prohibits burning. 
(Ord. No. 08-04, § 8.15, 4-8-2008; Ord. No. 08-05, § 8.16, 6-10-2008) 
Chapter 34 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Public buildings and grounds, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 281 et seq.; parks and other recreational and cultural resources, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 306 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 34-1-34-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - EXCAVATIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Trench safety standards, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 756.021 et seq. 

Sec. 34-19. - Permit requirement. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to make any excavation or opening in any street, alley or public right-of-way of the City without first having obtained a permit to do so, except in emergencies. 
(Code 1981, § 6.40; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-20. - Application for permit. 
    The application for a permit to make any excavation or opening in any of the streets, alleys, or public rights-of-way of the City, except for the purpose of setting utility poles, shall be made in writing to the City Administrator and shall state clearly the name of the street, alley, or right-of-way in which it is proposed to make such an opening; the exact location where such opening is proposed; the purpose for making the opening; the work schedule for making and repairing such opening; and the name and address of the person proposing to make such excavation or opening. Where the proposed excavation or opening is extensive, a plan for such work shall be submitted with the application. Such plan shall show adequate dimensions to indicate the exact location of the proposed excavation. 
(Code 1981, § 6.41; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-21. - Emergencies. 
    In case of emergencies where there is not sufficient time to make application for a permit, the police dispatcher shall be notified and given the same information described in section 34-20. 
(Code 1981, § 6.42; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-22. - Bond requirement. 
    The City Administrator shall estimate the probable cost of restoring the street surface to its original condition or better. Such estimate shall include the cost of select backfill materials, proper compaction of backfill, replacement or surfacing materials and cleanup. The applicant shall file a performance bond in the sum of 100 percent of the City Administrator's estimate. The permit shall not be in effect until such performance bond is filed with the City Administrator and accepted by the City Administrator. The performance bond shall be underwritten by a surety company or companies acceptable according to the latest list of companies holding certificates of authority from the Secretary of the Treasury of the United States and duly authorized to act under the laws of the state as surety. Bond will not be required where work is performed by bona fide fulltime employees, excluding contract labor or contractors of the gas, telephone and electric utilities. 
(Code 1981, § 6.43; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-23. - Permit issuance. 
    When the bond required in section 34-22 shall have been accepted by the City Administrator, the City Administrator shall then issue a written permit for the excavation or opening described in the application. The permit shall contain a statement of requirements to be met by the permittee in restoring surfaces of streets, alleys and rights-of-way and for protecting the public, as deemed necessary by the City Administrator. The permittee shall be fully responsible for safeguarding persons and property from damage or injury, and should the requirements prove to be inadequate under the circumstances. When the permit is issued the permittee may then proceed with the work in the exact location named in the application, and in no other place. 
(Code 1981, § 6.44; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-24. - Accessibility of permit. 
    The permittee shall keep a copy of the permit for excavation or opening streets, alleys or rights-of-way at all times at the site of the work, and such permit shall be accessible to the City Administrator or authorized representatives. 
(Code 1981, § 6.45; Ord. of 5-8-1983) 
Sec. 34-25. - Accomplishment of work. 
    All of the work done by the permittee in excavating or opening streets, alleys or rights-of-way, in backfilling excavations and in restoring street surfaces shall be in accordance with the terms of the permit issued by the City Administrator. The City Administrator shall be notified before commencement of work. The City Administrator shall issue whatever directions regarding the work as the City Administrator deems necessary to the end that the streets, alleys and rights-of-way of the City shall not be unduly disturbed and traffic thereon obstructed. The permittee shall comply with such directions. The directions given by the City Administrator shall not relieve the permittee from any responsibility for the protection of persons and property should such directions prove to be inadequate under the circumstances. 
(Code 1981, § 6.46; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-26. - Inspection and acceptance. 
    Upon completion of all work described in the permit, the permittee shall notify the director of public works, who will then inspect such work. If the permittee has failed to comply with the terms of the permit and has not left the street, alley or right-of-way clean and in a good state of repair satisfactory to the director of public works, then the director of public works shall give written notice to the permittee describing the work to be done and requiring such work to be completed within a specified time period. If the permittee fails to complete the required work within the specified time period, the director of public works shall call upon the surety to accomplish the required work. When the director of public works inspects the work and finds the street repaired in a satisfactory manner and cleaned of debris resulting from the work the director of public works shall accept such repair by written certificate to the permittee and the surety. 
(Code 1981, § 6.47; Ord. of 5-8-1973) 
Sec. 34-27. - Penalty. 
    Any person violating this article shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. 
Sec. 34-28. - Closure of city alley. 
    The City Council hereby abandons any and all public rights, title and interest, if any, to the alley, located going North and South between West O'Neal and West Orville and South 4 th and South 5 th streets. 
( Ord. No. 12-02, § 2, 3-13-2012 ) 
Secs. 34-29-34-39. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - USE OF PUBLIC RIGHT-OF-WAY 
DIVISION 1. - APPLICABLE TO ALL USERS IN GENERAL 

Sec. 34-40. - Title; application. 
(a)  This article may be known and cited as the Right-of-Way Management Ordinance for the City of Wills Point. 
(b)  The provisions of this article apply to all persons using the City's public rights-of-way and all work performed, and facilities installed within public rights-of-way. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-41. - Definitions. 
    All terms used in this article and not specifically defined herein, have the meaning provided in V.T.C.A., Local Government Code, Chapter 283 and 284. The following definitions apply in this article: 
    Abandon and its derivatives means the facilities installed in the public right-of- way that have been left in an unused or non-functioning condition for more than 120 consecutive calendar days, unless, after notice to the provider, the provider establishes to the city's reasonable satisfaction that the applicable facilities, or portion thereof, are still in active use. 
    Access line means (1) the transmission media within the rights-of-way extended to the end-user customer's premises network interface within the City that allows delivery of telecommunications service within the City; and (2) each termination point of a nonswitched telephone circuit consisting of transmission media connecting specific locations identified by, and provided to, the end user for the delivery of nonswitched telecommunications service within the City. Interoffice-transport and other transmission media that do not terminate at an end-user customer's network interface device are not access lines that would be separately identified and counted for the purposes of assessing the monthly line fee. 
    Antenna means communications equipment that transmits or receives electromagnetic radio frequency signals used in the provision of wireless services. 
    Applicable codes means: 
(a)  Uniform building, fire, electrical, plumbing, or mechanical codes adopted by a recognized national code organization; and 
(b)  Local amendments to those codes to the extent not inconsistent with Chapter 284. 
    Cable service means "cable service" as defined in the Cable Communications Policy Act of 1984, as amended, 47 U.S.C. § 532 et seq. 
    Certificated telecommunications provider means a person who has been issued a certificate of convenience and necessity, certificate of operating authority, or service provider certificate of operating authority by the Texas Public Utility Commission to offer local exchange telephone service or a person who provides voice service. 
    Chapter 284 means V.T.C.A., Local Government Code, Chapter 284. 
    City means the City of Wills Point, Texas. 
    City administrator means the city administrator of the City or his/her designee. 
    Closure means a complete or partial closing of one or more lanes of traffic of a thoroughfare for any period of time. 
    Construction means any of the following activities performed by any person within a public right-of-way: 
(1)  Installation, excavation, laying, placement, repair, upgrade, maintenance, or relocation of facilities or other improvements, whether temporary or permanent. 
(2)  Modification or alteration to any surface, subsurface, or aerial space within the public right-of-way. 
(3)  Performance, restoration, or repair of pavement cuts or excavations. 
(4)  Reconstruction of any of the work described in paragraphs (1) through (3) above. 
(5)  Other similar construction work. 
    Collocate and collocation means the installation, mounting, maintenance, modification, operation, or replacement of network nodes in a public right-of-way on or adjacent to a pole. 
    Consumer price index means the annual revised Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers for Texas, as published by the federal Bureau of Labor Statistics. 
    Concealment or Camouflaged means any wireless facility or pole that is covered, blended, painted, disguised, camouflaged, or otherwise concealed such that the wireless facility blends into the surrounding environment and is visually unobtrusive as allowed as a condition for City advance approval under Chapter 284, Sec. 284.105 in Historic or Design Districts. Concealment includes but is not limited to covering with a façade, designs that blend with the surrounding character of an area, paint that matches surrounding poles, disguising with landscaping, or locating underground. 
    Decorative pole means a streetlight pole specially designed and placed for aesthetic purposes and on which no appurtenances or attachments, other than specially designed informational or directional signage or temporary holiday or special event attachments have been placed or are permitted to be placed according to City Code. 
    Design district means an area that is zoned, or otherwise designated by City code, and for which the City maintains and enforces unique design and aesthetic standards. 
    Design manual means the design requirements for specific types of facilities, including any adopted design manuals, the City's unified development code, adopted construction codes and any other City requirements. 
    Disaster emergency or disaster or emergency means an imminent, impending, or actual natural or humanly induced situation wherein the health, safety, or welfare of the residents of the City is threatened, and includes, but is not limited to any declaration of emergency by city, state or federal governmental authorities. 
    Distributed antenna system or DAS shall be included as a type of "network node." 
    Easement means any public easement or other compatible use created by dedication, or by other means, to the City for public utility purposes or any other purpose whatsoever. "Easement" shall include a private easement used for the provision of utilities. 
    Facilities means any and all network nodes, micro network nodes, transport facilities, equipment cabinets, node support poles, duct spaces, manholes, poles, conduits, underground and overhead passageways, and other equipment, structures, plant, and appurtenances and all transmission media used for the provision of wireless service or telecommunication service. 
    Federal Communications Commission or FCC means the Federal Administrative Agency, or lawful successor, authorized to oversee cable television and other multi-channel regulation on a national level. 
    Highway right-of-way means the right-of-way adjacent to a state or federal highway. 
    Historic district or historic area means an area that is zoned or otherwise designated as a historic area or historic district under municipal, state, or federal law. 
    Law means common law or a federal, state, or local law, statute, code, rule, regulation, order, or ordinance. 
    Licensee or applicant means any person with a license or authorized under state law, or the person applying for or receiving a permit to perform construction within the City's right-of-way and the owner of the utility within the right-of-way under the terms and conditions set forth herein. The term includes: (i) any officer, director, partner, manager, superintendent, or other authorized person exercising control over or on behalf of the licensee; and (ii) any contractor or subcontractor of the licensee, for purposes of compliance with the provisions of this article and the traffic control, construction, and maintenance requirements of this article. 
    Line fee means a monthly fee to be applied to each access line for the calculation of the total amount to be paid to the City as a rights-of-way fee. 
    Local means within the geographical boundaries of the City. 
    Location means the City-approved and lawfully permitted location for the network node and/or node support poles. 
    Macro tower means a guyed or self-supported pole or monopole with height parameters not greater than the lesser of (i) 55 feet, or (ii) ten feet higher than the tallest existing utility pole located within 500 linear feet of the new pole in the same public right-of-way and that supports or is capable of supporting antennas, as the prescribed by Chapter 284, Section 284.103, as may be amended. 
    Mayor means the Mayor for the City. 
    Micro network node means a network node that is not larger in dimension than 24 inches in length, 15 inches in width, and 12 inches in height, and that has an exterior antenna, if any, not longer than 11 inches. 
    Municipally owned utility pole means a utility pole owned or operated by a municipally owned utility, as defined by V.T.C.A., Utilities Code, § 11.003, and located in a public right-of-way. 
    Municipal park or park means an area that is zoned or otherwise designated by the City as a public park for the purpose of recreational activity. 
    MUTCD means Manual of Uniform Traffic Control Devices. 
    Network node means equipment at a fixed location that enables wireless communications between user equipment and a communications network. The term includes: (i) equipment associated with wireless communications; (ii) a radio transceiver, an antenna, a battery-only backup power supply, and comparable equipment, regardless of technological configuration; and (iii) coaxial or fiber-optic cable that is immediately adjacent to and directly associated with a particular collocation; and does not include: (i) an electric generator; (ii) a pole; or (iii) a macro tower. 
    Network provider means a wireless service provider; or a person that does not provide wireless services and that is not an electric utility but builds or installs on behalf of a wireless service provider: (i) network nodes; or (ii) node support poles or any other structure that supports or is capable of supporting a network node. 
    Node support pole means a pole installed by a network provider for the primary purpose of supporting a network node. 
    Permit means a written authorization for the use of the public right-of-way, including collocation on a service pole required from the City before a network provider or provider or person, as those terms are defined herein, may perform an action or initiate, continue, or complete a project over which the City has police power authority. 
    Permit holder means any person that has applied for or been issued a permit pursuant to the terms of this article. 
    Person means a natural person, a corporation, a limited liability company, a joint venture, a business trust, an estate, a trust, a partnership, an association, a company, a firm, a joint stock company or association, or any other legal entity. 
    Pole means a service pole, municipally owned utility pole, node support pole, or utility pole. 
    Private easement means an easement or other real property right that is only for the benefit of the grantor and grantee and their successors and assigns. 
    Project means any construction or placement of any structure or thing within any public right-of-way. 
    Provider has the same meaning as "network provider." To the extent allowed by law, provider also means a person that does not deliver telecommunications service within the City, but who uses, constructs or maintains facilities or transmission media within the public rights-of-way. 
    Public right-of-way means the area on, below, or above a public roadway, highway, street, public sidewalk, alley, waterway, or utility easement in which the City has an interest. The term does not include (i) a private easement, or (ii) the airwaves above the public right-of-way with regard to wireless telecommunications. 
    Public right-of-way rate means an annual rental charge paid by a network provider to a municipality related to the construction, maintenance, or operation of network nodes within a public right-of-way in the City. 
    Public right-of-way management ordinance means an ordinance that complies with Chapter 284, Subchapter C. 
    School means an educational institution that offers a course of instruction for students in one or more grades from kindergarten through grade 12. 
    Service pole means a pole, other than a municipally owned utility pole, owned or operated by the City and located in a public right-of-way, including: (i) a pole that supports traffic control functions; (ii) a structure for signage; (iii) a pole that supports lighting, other than a decorative pole; and (iv) a pole or similar structure owned or operated by the City and supporting only network nodes. 
    Service provider means any electric utility, gas utility, telecommunications company, cable company, water utility, storm water utility, or wastewater utility, regardless of whether the service provider is publicly or privately owned or required to operate within the city pursuant to a franchise. 
    Sidewalk means that portion of a public right-of-way improved and designated for and ordinarily used for pedestrian travel or pedestrian and bicycle travel. 
    Small cell shall be included as a type of "network node." 
    Street means only the paved portion of the right-of-way used for vehicular travel, being the area between the inside of the curb to the inside of the opposite curb, or the area between the two parallel edges of the paved roadway for vehicular travel where there is no curb. A "street" is generally part of, but smaller in width than the width of the entire right-of-way, while a right-of-way may include sidewalks and utility easements, a "street" does not. A "street" does not include the curb or the sidewalk, if either are present at the time of a permit application or if added later. 
    Substantially similar means a replacement or upgrade that does not include replacement of an existing node support pole nor defeat existing concealment elements of a node support pole; and a new or upgraded network node, including the antenna or other equipment element, will not be more than ten percent larger than the existing node, provided that the increase may not result in the node exceeding the size limitations provided by the City's design manual; and the new or upgraded pole will not be more than ten percent higher than the existing pole, provided that the increase may not result in the pole exceeding the applicable height limitations prescribed by the City's design manual. 
    Supervisor means the supervisor of public works or any other person designated by the City Administrator to administer this article. 
    SWPPP shall mean Storm Water Pollution Prevention Plan. 
    TAS means Texas Accessibility Standards. 
    Telecommunications service means the transmittal of voice, data, image, graphics and other communications between or among points by wire, fiber optics, or other similar facilities, as well as the rental, lease, or furnishing of the facilities to accomplish such transmittal, but does not include transmissions for long distance purposes (interLATA and intraLATA) or any "wireless service" as defined by law. 
    Telecommunications service provider means any person that supplies telecommunications service to others within the City's corporate limits in exchange for money or other value. 
    Telecommunications utility means "telecommunications utility" as used in the Public Utility Regulatory Act, V.T.C.A., Utilities Code § 51.002(11). 
    Traffic signal means any device, whether manually, electrically, or mechanically operated by which traffic is alternately directed to stop and to proceed. 
    Transmission media means any and all of the cables, fibers, wires or other physical devices owned, maintained or placed by a user to transmit and/or receive communication signals, whether analog, digital or of other characteristics, and whether for voice, data or other purposes. 
    Transport facility means each transmission path physically within a public right-of- way, extending with a physical line from a network node directly to the network, for the purpose of providing backhaul for network nodes. 
    Underground requirement area means an area where poles, overhead wires, and associated overhead or above ground structures have been removed and buried or have been approved for burial underground pursuant to municipal ordinances, zoning regulations, state law, private deed restrictions, and other public or private restrictions, that prohibit installing aboveground structures in a public right-of-way. 
    User means a person, organization or entity that owns, places, installs, maintains, or uses facilities within the public right-of-way or street, depending upon the context. 
    Utility pole means a pole that provides: (i) electric distribution with a voltage rating of not more than 34.5 kilovolts; or (ii) services of a telecommunications provider, as defined by V.T.C.A., Utilities Code, § 51.002, Utilities Code. 
    Wireless facilities mean "micro network nodes," "network nodes," and "node support poles" as defined in Texas Local Government Code Chapter 284. 
    Wireless service means any service, using licensed or unlicensed wireless spectrum, including the use of Wi-Fi, whether at a fixed location or mobile, provided to the public using a network node. 
    Wireless service provider means a person that provides wireless service to the public. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-42. - Authorization for use of public right-of-way. 
(a)  The City Administrator, supervisor, or their designee is authorized to administer and enforce the provisions of this article. The City Administrator, supervisor or his/her/their designee is authorized to enter upon a construction site for which a permit is granted under this article or, where necessary, upon private property adjacent to the construction site, for purposes of inspection to determine compliance with the permit or this article. 
(b)  The City's authorization or an agreement shall be required to use the public right-of-way, except when clearly preempted by state law. If any state law authorizing use of the public right-of-way is struck down, pre-empted, declared to be invalid or void, in whole or in part, the user relying upon such law for authorization shall seek separate authorization from the City or shall cease using the public right-of-way. 
(c)  After issuance of any permit, the user of the public right-of-way shall be and remain a mere licensee. Neither this ordinance, nor any permit granted under this ordinance, shall constitute an assignment of any of the City's rights to the public right-of-way. 
(d)  This ordinance does not in any way limit the City's right to locate, operate, maintain or remove City equipment or property in the manner that the City deems appropriate. 
(e)  When an agreement is required to use the public right-of-way, a permit for the construction work may not be issued until the agreement is obtained. 
(f)  The city's authorization to a person, provider, service provider, network provider, certificated telecommunications provider, wireless service provider or user does not allow use of third party facilities in the public right-of-way. 
(g)  The City's authorization to use its public right-of-way does not extend to the use of any other City property or facilities. 
(h)  The City may impose additional requirements on the activities of a person, provider, service provider, network provider, certificated telecommunications provider, wireless service provider or user in the public right-of-way to the extent that the regulations are reasonably necessary to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the public. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-43. - Registration and construction permits. 
    No person shall commence or continue with the construction or installation of any facility within the City rights-of-way, except as provided by this article or as provided by other City permits or written agreements with the City. 
(a)  Registration required. All users of the right-of-way must register annually with the City. Registration must be renewed and paid to the City Secretary by January 1st of every year. Registration and permits will be issued in the name of the person who will own the facilities. Registration shall include: 
1.  The name of the user of the right-of-way; 
2.  The name, address, and telephone number of the persons who will be contact person(s) for the user; 
3.  The name(s) and telephone number of an emergency contact who shall be available 24 hours a day; 
4.  The location, including exact coordinates by GPS, of all facilities located in the rights-of-way; and 
5.  A description of each facility located in the rights-of-way. 
(b)  Construction permit required. Unless otherwise provided by this article, no person shall perform any construction or installation of facilities in the rights-of-way without first obtaining a construction permit. The permit will be in the name of the person who will own the proposed facilities. The permit must be completed and signed by a representative of the owner of the proposed facilities. The permit shall state to whom it is issued, location of work, location of proposed facilities, estimated dates and times the work is to take place and any other conditions set out by the City Administrator or his/her designee, or other decision making body when applicable. 
1.  Information required for a permit. The person requesting a permit will provide the City Administrator or his/her designee with documentation describing: 
i.  The proposed, approximate location with GPS coordinates and route of all facilities to be constructed or installed and the applicant's plan for right-of-way construction. 
ii.  Engineering plans provided on a drawing scale not smaller than one inch equals 100 feet unless otherwise approved by the City Administrator. 
iii.  Description of all existing public and private utilities in close proximity to applicant's proposed route. 
iv.  Description of the applicant's proposed installation, such as pipe size, number of interducts, valves, and other related information. 
v.  Description of plans to remove and replace pavement or drainage works in streets. Plans submitted must conform to the City's standard construction requirements, City Code of Ordinances and the City's applicable building codes. 
vi.  Drawings of any bores, trenches, handholes, manholes, switch gear, transformers, pedestals, and similar items including depth. 
vii.  Manholes of the type applicant plans to use or access. 
viii.  Complete legend of drawings submitted by applicant, which may be provided by reference to previously submitted documents. 
ix.  Three sets of engineering plans must be submitted with permit application. 
x.  The construction and installation methods to be employed for the protection of existing facilities, fixtures, and facilities within or adjacent to the right-of-way, and the estimated dates and times work will occur, all of which (methods, dates, and times) are subject to approval of the City Administrator or his/her designee; 
xi.  A traffic control plan per the MUTCD for any proposed traffic routing or proposed lane closures; 
xii.  A stormwater pollution prevention plan and trench safety plan, if applicable; 
xiii.  Three sets of scaled dimensioned drawings of proposed attachments to poles, as well as other proposed equipment associated with the permit application, indicating the spacing from existing curb, public right-of-way line, driveways, sidewalks, light poles, off street pathways, and any other poles or appurtenances, together with an existing aerial and street view of the proposed location; 
xiv.  For installation of any proposed pole, a sectional detail showing the depth of anchor, scaled dimension drawings of the proposed pole, as well as any other proposed equipment associated with the proposed installation, indicating spacing from existing curb, public right-of-way line, driveways, sidewalks, light poles, off street pathways and any other poles or appurtenances; 
xv.  Construction and installation methods to be employed for protection of existing structures, fixtures, and facilities within or adjacent to the public right-of-way and the dates and times the work will occur, all of which are subject to approval of the City Administrator, Supervisor, City Engineer or their designee; 
xvi.  For any proposed work that involves installation of facilities that will use radio frequencies, evidence in a form acceptable to the City Administrator, showing that the proposed installation will be compatible with the City's systems and will not cause interference with the City's public safety radio system, traffic signal light system, or other City communications systems or components; 
xvii.  A copy of the certificate issued by the Public Utility Commission for telecommunications, cable service providers, and video service providers; 
xviii.  Proof of compliance with private deed restrictions or other private restrictions where applicable; 
xix.  If the project lies within a highway right-of-way, evidence of a permit from the state or federal authority; 
xx.  If the project lies within property owned by a railroad company, evidence of written authorization from the railroad company; 
xxi.  If the project is for installation of network node facilities and/or network node service poles, a map or document showing the intended network node location and its distance from a designated historic landmark, park, or school, utility pole, node support pole, and other network nodes on a service pole, if any, and depicting the sidewalks, and ramps onto sidewalks required by applicable Codes, TAS, or other law, including the Americans with Disabilities Act, and paved street surface and utility easements; 
xxii.  Proof or a certificate of compliance with all applicable regulations of the Federal Communications Commission; 
xxiii.  Proof or certification that the proposed facilities will be placed into active commercial service by or for a network provider or user within 60 days after the date the construction and final testing of the facilities is completed as provided in V.T.C.A., Local Government Code, Chapter 284. An updated certification of active service must be submitted annually, by no later than January 1 st , with or prior to payment of the applicable annual fee(s); and 
xxiv.  Proof of insurance or net worth as required. 
2.  Access to site. All construction and installation in the right-of-way shall be in accordance with the permit for the facilities. The City Administrator or his/her designee shall be provided access to the work and to such further information as may reasonably be required to ensure compliance with the permit. 
3.  Plans at site. A copy of the construction permit and approved engineering plans shall be maintained at the construction site and made available for inspection by the City Administrator, supervisor or his/her/their designee at all times when construction or installation work is occurring. 
4.  Timeliness. All construction or installation work authorized by permit must be completed in the time specified in the construction permit. If the work cannot be completed in the specified time periods, the permit holder may request an extension from the City Administrator or his/her designee. A permit issued under this article is valid for the time period specified by the City Administrator, based upon the estimated time to complete the work. Upon the written request of the permit holder, the City Administrator may grant additional time to complete the work under the permit. If the person receiving the permit fails to act upon the permit within 180 days of issuance, the permit shall be invalid and the person will be required to obtain another permit. 
5.  Approval. Unless otherwise provided by this article, requests for permits shall be approved or disapproved by the City Administrator or his/her designee within a reasonable time of receiving all the necessary information. The City Administrator or his/her designee shall use his/her best efforts to approve or disapprove a request for permit as soon as possible. 
6.  Pre-construction meeting. The City Administrator or user may request a pre-construction meeting.
