(c)  Exception to construction permit requirement. The following activities shall not be required to obtain a permit under this article. 
1.  Emergencies. Emergency responses related to existing facilities may be undertaken without first obtaining a permit; however, the City Administrator must be notified in writing within two business days of any construction related to an emergency response. A reasonably detailed description of the work performed in the right-of-way and an updated map of any facilities moved shall be provided as soon as practicable; 
2.  Routine maintenance. Except as specifically provided otherwise by this article, the installation of facilities necessary to initiate utility, water, wastewater or other service to a customer's property or the repair or maintenance of existing facilities, unless such repair or maintenance requires the breaking of pavement, excavation in the right-of-way, or the closure of a public traffic lane for greater than two hours, are not required to obtain a permit under this article; 
3.  Exempt by law. Maintenance or replacement activities exempt by law from obtaining a permit; 
4.  Existing facilities. The repair, replacement, or maintenance of an existing telephone line, natural gas line, electric line, cable television or telecommunications line, irrigation line, or other existing pipe, cable, or facility lawfully located in the public right-of-way, if the repair, replacement, or maintenance does not require the digging up, breaking up, cutting, excavation, drilling or tunneling under or the removal, modification, or excavation of a public street, sidewalk, water or sewer line, or other City-owned improvement, except as may otherwise be provided in state law; 
5.  Existing vegetation. The repair, replacement, or maintenance of existing trees, shrubs, flowers, grass, vegetation, berms, decorative landscaping, or watering systems that are lawfully located in the public-right-way, if the repair, replacement, or maintenance does not require the digging up, breaking up, cutting, excavation, drilling or tunneling under, or the removal, modification, or excavation, of a public street, sidewalk, water or sewer line, or other City-owned improvement; 
6.  Work for City. Any work performed for the City under a contract with the City; or 
7.  Sign permit work. Any work required to install a sign on a public right-of-way if the applicant has received a sign permit from the City pursuant to Chapter 30 of the City Code of Ordinances and has complied with the requirements of this article. 
(d)  Consolidated permit application. A network provider that will install or collocate multiple network nodes inside the City limits may file a consolidated permit application with the City for no more than 30 network nodes. 
(e)  FCC/PUC documents. Copies of petitions, applications, and reports submitted by the permit holder to the Federal Communications Commission or the Texas Public Utility Commission shall be provided to the City upon request. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-44. - Insurance, liability and indemnity. 
(a)  Insurance. An applicant must provide proof of liability insurance in the amount of $1,000,000.00, as approved by the City Administrator or his/her designee. Such requirements may be waived by the City Administrator or his/her designee, if the applicant provides acceptable evidence of self-insurance backed by assets equal to but not less than a net worth in the amount of at least $5,000,000.00 as approved by the City Administrator or his/her designee and/or the City Mayor or his/her designee. 
1.  The coverage provided shall be on an "occurrence" basis and shall include coverage for personal injury, contractual liability, premises liability, medical damages, underground, explosion, and collapse hazards. 
2.  Each policy must include a cancellation provision in which the insurance company is required to notify the City in writing not fewer than 30 days before canceling, failing to renew, or reducing policy limits. 
3.  The applicant shall file the required original certificate of insurance prior to any commencement of work. The certificate shall state the policy number; name of the insurance company; name and address of the agent or authorized representative of the insurance company; name, address and telephone number of insured; policy expiration date; and specific coverage amounts. 
4.  Applicant shall file a surety bond from a surety company authorized to do business in the State of Texas in the amount of $15,000.00 to guarantee the restoration of the right-of-way in the event the applicant leaves a job site in the right-of-way unfinished, incomplete, or unsafe. Such requirement for a surety bond may be waived by the City Administrator or his/her designee upon a showing of financial responsibility by the applicant. 
5.  The applicant agrees to waive its right to subrogation against the City and its officers and employees for bodily injury (including death), property damage, or any other loss. 
6.  The insurance coverage required by this article is considered primary insurance in regard to the City and its officers, employees, and elected representatives. Proof of insurance in the form of an original industry standard certificate of insurance showing the City as an additional insured must be provided to the City Administrator prior to any commencement of work by the applicant. The certificate of insurance must be executed by the insurer or its authorized agent and must state specific coverage, limits, and expiration dates in accordance with the requirements of this article. 
7.  The applicant shall make available to the City Administrator, upon request, a copy of the insurance policy, including any endorsements, riders, and amendments to the policy and any statements respecting coverage under the policy. 
(b)  Liability. A person owning facilities in the public right-of-way is responsible and liable for acts or omissions of its employees, temporary employees, officers, directors, consultants, agents, affiliates, subsidiaries, contractors, and subcontractors involving the installation of all facilities in the public right-of- way as if such acts or omissions were the acts or omissions of the person owning the facilities in the public right-of-way. 
(c)  Indemnity. The following indemnity provisions apply to a service provider, provider, or network provider and are express terms of a permit issued under this article: 
1.  A licensee who is a certificated telecommunications provider as defined in V.T.C.A., Local Government Code, Chapter 283, as amended, or a network provider as defined in V.T.C.A., Local Government Code, Chapter 284, as amended, shall provide to the City the indemnity provided in V.T.C.A., Local Government Code, § 283.057, as amended. 
2.  A licensee, other than a certificated telecommunications provider or network provider described in paragraph 1. of this subsection, expressly agrees to fully and completely defend, indemnify, and hold harmless the City and its officers, agents, and employees, against any and all claims, lawsuits, judgments, costs, and expenses for personal injury (including death), property damage or other harm for which recovery of damages is sought, suffered by any person or persons, that may arise out of or be occasioned by any negligent, grossly negligent, wrongful or strictly liable act or omission of the licensee or its agents, employees, or contractors, in the performance of work or activity pursuant to the permit issued under this article, regardless of whether or not the negligence, gross negligence, wrongful act, or fault of the City or its officers, agents or employees, contributes in any way to the damage, injury, or other harm. Expenses shall include any reasonable and necessary attorney's fees and court costs. Nothing in this paragraph may be construed as waiving any governmental immunity available to the City under state law. This provision is solely for the benefit of the licensee and the City and is not intended to create or grant any rights, contractual or otherwise, in or to any other third party or person. 
The City shall give the permit holder prompt written notice of any claim for which the City seeks indemnification. The permit holder shall have the right to investigate, defend and compromise any such claim. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-45. - Relocation, conformance, restoration and removal of facilities. 
A.  Removal or relocation required for city project. 
(a)  Within 90 days after receiving written notice from the City and as allowed by state and federal law, any person owning facilities/network provider located in the public right-of-way must, as directed by the City and at the person's sole cost, temporarily or permanently remove, relocate, change or alter the position of any of the facilities that are in the public right-of-way whenever the City determines that the removal, relocation, change or alteration is necessary: 
1.  For the construction, repair, maintenance, installation, completion, relocation, replacement, or widening of any City improvement, street, facilities, or equipment, in or upon the public right-of-way; or 
2.  The facilities have become obsolete. 
(a1)  This subsection complies with Chapter 284, Section 284.107. 
(b)  Facilities that are not conformed within the 90-day notice period will be deemed abandoned and the City will not be liable for any damage to or destruction or removal of the facilities, or for any interruption or termination of service through the facilities caused by activity of the City described in this section. As allowed by state and federal law, a person owning facilities/network provider located in the public right-of-way must remove its facilities that have been abandoned regardless of whether it receives notice from the City. Removal must be completed immediately if the City notifies the person immediate removal is necessary to protect public health, safety and welfare. 
(c)  The relocation or removal of facilities must comply with state and federal law and this article. The facility owner/network provider understands and acknowledges that the City may require its facilities be removed or relocated from the public right-of-way for the construction, completion, repair, widening, relocation, or maintenance of, or used in connection with, any City construction or maintenance project of a street or public right-of-way to enhance the traveling public's use for travel and transportation. 
(d)  If a person does not remove or relocate its facilities as required under subsection (a) of this section, the City may remove the facilities at the person's sole cost and expense, without further notice to the person. Within 30 days after receiving an invoice from the City, the person shall reimburse the City for its reasonable expenses incurred in the removal or relocation of the facilities. 
B.  Removal required by city for safety and imminent danger purposes. 
(a)  If the City administrator or his/her designee determines that there is imminent danger to the public health, safety and welfare, the City Administrator may immediately disconnect, remove or relocate a facility owner's/network provider's facilities in the public right-of-way at the facility owner's/network provider's sole cost. The facility owner/network provider shall reimburse the City for its reasonable expenses incurred in the removal or relocation of the facilities within 30 days following receipt of an invoice from the City. 
(b)  Facility owner/network provider shall, at its sole cost and expense, promptly disconnect, remove, or relocate the applicable facilities within the time frame and in the manner required by the City Administrator if the City Administrator reasonably determines that the disconnection, removal, or relocation of any part of the facilities (i) is necessary to protect the public health, safety, welfare, or City property, (ii) the facilities, or portion thereof, is adversely affecting proper operation of streetlights or City property, or (c) facility owner/network provider fails to obtain all applicable licenses, permits, and certifications required by law for its facilities, or use of any location under applicable law in strict accordance with the City's Code of Ordinances, and other applicable laws, except to the extent not consistent with Chapter 284. 
(c)  The City Administrator shall provide 90 days written notice to the facility owner/network provider before removing facilities or other equipment under this section, unless there is imminent danger to the public health, safety, and welfare. 
C.  Removal or relocation by facility owner/network provider. 
(a)  If a person owning a facility/network provider in the public right-of-way removes or relocates the facility at its discretion, the person shall notify the City in writing not less than ten business days prior to the removal or relocation. A relocation must be performed at the person's sole cost and expense. The person shall obtain all permits required, if any, for the removal or relocation of the person's facilities prior to the removal or relocation. 
(b)  A person owning facilities/network provider in the public right-of-way must restore and repair damage to the public right-of-way caused by the relocation or removal of its facilities within ten calendar days of the removal or relocation at the person' sole cost and expense. The public right-of-way must be restored to substantially the same condition as it was immediately before the removal or relocation, including restoration or replacement of damaged trees, shrubs, or other vegetation. Such repair, restoration and replacement shall be subject to the sole reasonable approval of the City Administrator or his/her designee. 
(c)  A person owning facilities/network provider in the public right-of-way shall remove its facilities when such facilities are abandoned regardless of whether or not it receives notice from the City. Unless the City sends notice that removal must be completed immediately to ensure public health, safety, and welfare, the removal must be completed within 90 days of the facilities being abandoned or within 90 days of receipt of written notice from the City. When facility owner, network provider removes, or abandons permanent structures in the right-of-way, the facility owner, network provider shall notify the City Administrator in writing of such removal or abandonment and shall file with the City Administrator the location and description of each facility removed or abandoned. The City Administrator may require the facility owner, network provider to complete additional remedial measures necessary for public safety and the integrity of the right-of-way. 
(d)  The City will not issue any refunds for amounts paid by a person for a permit or application for the facilities that are removed or relocated. 
D.  Restoration of property. 
(a)  Restoration of affected property required. Users of the right-of-way shall restore property affected by construction in the right-of-way to a condition that is equal to or better than the condition of the property prior to the performance of the work. This includes, but is not limited to, replacing all natural ground cover with an equal or better type of ground cover damaged during work, either by sodding or seeding, as directed by City Administrator. 
(b)  Restoration requirements. Restoration shall be to the reasonable satisfaction of the City Administrator. The restoration shall include, but not be limited to: 
1.  Installation of all manholes and handholes, as required; 
2.  All bore pits, potholes, trenches, or any other holes shall be covered or barricaded daily; 
3.  Leveling of all trenches and backhoe lines; and 
4.  Restoration of excavation site to City specifications. 
(c)  Locator flags. All locator flags shall be removed during the cleanup process by the permit holder or his/her contractor at the completion of the work. 
E.  No allocation of city funds for removal and storage. The City has no funds appropriated to pay for the cost of any removal or storage of facilities as authorized under this article, and no other monies are allocated. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-46. - Stop work orders; denial or revocation of permit; appeals. 
(a)  If a person violates a provision of this article, or applicable codes and ordinances, the City Administrator or his/her designee may issue a written stop work order to the violator directing any work or activity authorized to be done under a permit to cease until the violation is corrected. Upon receiving a stop work order, the permit holder must immediately cause all work authorized under the permit to stop, but may take steps necessary to secure the site. 
(b)  The City Administrator or his/her designee may revoke a permit for a violation of this article. To revoke a permit, the City Administrator or his/her designee must send or deliver written notice of a violation to the permit holder ordering the violation to be corrected within a specified time. If the permit holder fails to correct the violation as directed, the City Administrator or his/her designee may revoke the permit by giving notice to the permit holder in writing. 
(c)  Any person may appeal the denial or revocation of a permit, the interpretation or application of a requirement of this article, the issuance of a stop work order or notice of violation, or other requirement or action imposed under this article by the City Administrator or his/her designee. The appeal must be submitted in writing to the City Administrator or his/her designee within 72 hours of the action being appealed. The City Administrator or his/her designee will promptly review the facts and issue a written determination. 
(d)  The revocation, denial and appeal provisions in this section govern over any other conflicting provision in this Code of Ordinances, except as provided by Chapter 284 provisions found in division 2 of this article. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-47. - Violations and Penalty. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any person to knowingly construct, place, maintain, or operate any line, wire, pipe, conduit, equipment, pole, structure, or facility in a public right-of-way or other public property for the purpose of providing water, wastewater, electrical, natural gas, or other service for which use of the public right-of-way is not authorized by state law, to any person, without first receiving the consent of the City Administrator or his/her designee. The City may, as a condition of giving its consent, require the person requesting such use to enter into a written agreement with the City containing the conditions under which the use of the public rights-of-way will be permitted. To the extent any provision contained in this Section conflicts with V.T.C.A, Local Government Code, Chapter 284, such provision shall not apply, shall be void and shall be struck from this Section. 
(b)  Except in cases of emergency, it is unlawful for any person to knowingly dig up, break, cut, excavate, drill or tunnel in or on any public right-of-way without first obtaining a right-of-way work permit from the City. 
(c)  It is unlawful for any person to knowingly install or place any facilities in a public right-of-way or make use of the public right-of-way for any purpose not authorized by state law. 
(d)  It is unlawful for any person to knowingly violate a provision of this article. 
(e)  It is unlawful for any person doing work under a permit to violate a provision of the permit. 
(f)  It is unlawful for any person to continue work under a permit after receiving a stop work order or receiving notice that a stop work order has been issued or to resume the work or activity until the City Administrator or Supervisor withdraws the stop work order. 
(g)  Each unauthorized use of the public right-of-way or other public property is a separate offense. And each day a violation continues is a separate offense. Any person violating this article, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to the penalties in section 1-12. A culpable mental state is not required to prove an offense under this article. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-48-34-49. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CERTIFICATED TELECOMMUNICATIONS PROVIDERS AND NETWORK PROVIDERS 

Sec. 34-50. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this division is to: 
1.  Assist the City in the management of the public rights-of-way; 
2.  Govern the use and occupancy of the rights-of-way by telecommunications and network providers; 
3.  Secure fair and reasonable compensation for the use and occupancy of the public rights-of-way by all persons, providers, users in a nondiscriminatory and competitively neutral manner; and 
4.  Assist the City in its efforts to protect the public health, safety and welfare. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-51. - General terms. 
(a)  Authority required/non-exclusive use. All certificated telecommunications providers and/or network providers must provide evidence that the certificated telecommunications provider and/or network provider has acquired authorization from the Texas Public Utility Commission pursuant to state law, prior to obtaining a permit to use the public right-of-way. The right to use and occupy the public right-of-way shall not be exclusive, and the City shall have the right to exercise its police powers and manage its public right-of-way, based upon all other state or federal laws. The City reserves the right to grant franchises, licenses, easements or permissions to use the rights-of-way within the City to any person as the City, in its sole discretion, may determine to be in the public interest. 
(b)  Permit for installation of wireless facilities. A network provider may not install network nodes or node support equipment in any public right-of-way until a permit to do so has been issued by the City pursuant to the requirements set forth in section 34-43(a)-(e) of this article. 
(c)  Prohibited or restricted areas for wireless facilities in the right-of-way. 
1.  Municipal parks and residential areas. A network provider may not install a new node support pole in a municipal park, unless permission is given by the City Administrator; or in a right-of-way that contains a street that is equal to or less than 50 feet wide, measuring curb-to-curb, and is adjacent to developed or undeveloped single-family residential lots, other multifamily residential area or land that is designated for residential use by zoning or deed restrictions. 
2.  Historic districts and design districts. A network provider must obtain advance written approval from the City before collocating network nodes or installing node support poles in a design district with decorative poles or in an area of the City zoned or otherwise designated as a design district or historic district. As a condition for approval of network nodes or node support poles in design districts with decorative poles or in an historic district, the City shall require reasonable design or concealment measures for the network nodes or node support poles. All network providers must comply with the City's Design Manual for the Installation of Network Nodes and Node Support Poles on file with the City Secretary in the City office. 
(d)  Notification requirements for certificated telecommunications providers and network providers. A certificated telecommunications provider and/or network provider shall notify the City Administrator or his/her designee of any sale, transfer, merger or assignment of the ownership or control of a certificated telecommunications provider's or network provider's business within 30 days of such sale, transfer, merger or assignment. A certificated telecommunications provider and/or network provider shall also maintain and provide current point-of-contact information with the City Administrator or his/her designee at all times during which the certificated telecommunications provider and/or network provider uses the right-of-way. 
(e)  The provisions found in section 34-45 of this article pertaining to relocation, conformance and removal of facilities shall apply to all persons, facility owners, telecommunications providers, network providers, and/or users performing work under this division. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-52. - Installation, inspections and construction. 
(a)  Installation. A network provider shall, at its own cost and expense, install the micro network node, network node, node support poles and related ground equipment in a good and workmanlike manner and in accordance with the requirements promulgated by the City in its Design Manual for the Installation of Network Nodes and Node Support Poles, as such may be amended from time to time. Network provider's work shall be subject to the regulation, control and direction of the City Administrator. All work done in connection with the installation, operation, maintenance, repair, modification, and/or replacement of the micro network node, network node, node support poles and related ground equipment shall be in compliance with all applicable laws, ordinances, codes, rules and regulations of the City, applicable county, the state, and the United States. 
(b)  Inspections. The City Administrator, or his/her designee, may perform visual inspections of any micro network node, network node, node support pole or related ground equipment located in the public right-of-way as the City Administrator deems appropriate without notice. If the inspection requires physical contact with the micro network node, network node, node support poles or related ground equipment, the City Administrator shall provide written notice to the network provider within five business days of the planned inspection. The network provider may have a representative present during such inspection. 
(c)  Construction requirements. Except where otherwise provided by state law, a network provider shall construct and maintain facilities in accordance with the City's Design Manual for the Installation of Network Nodes and Node Support Poles to ensure facilities do not: 
1.  Obstruct, impede, or hinder the usual travel or public safety on a public right-of-way; 
2.  Obstruct the legal use of a public right-of-way by other utility providers; 
3.  Violate applicable codes; 
4.  Violate or conflict with the City's public right-of-way design specifications; or 
5.  Violate the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990. 
(d)  Permit limited. A permit provided under this division does not provide authorization for attachment of network nodes on poles and other structures owned or operated by investor-owned electric utilities, as defined by V.T.C.A., Utilities Code, § 31.002, electric cooperatives, telephone cooperatives, as defined by V.T.C.A., Utilities Code, § 162.003, or wireless providers, as defined by V.T.C.A., Utilities Code, § 51.002. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-53. - Application review process. 
(a)  Determination of application completeness. The City shall determine whether the permit application is complete and notify the applicant of that determination. The City shall identify the missing information if the City determines that the application is not complete: 
1.  For network nodes and node support poles: no later than 30 business days after the date the City receives the permit application. 
2.  For a transport facility: no later than ten business days after the date the City receives the permit application. 
(b)  Approval or denial of application. The City shall approve or deny a completed application after the date it is submitted to the City: 
1.  For network nodes: No later than 60 business days after the date the City Administrator receives the complete application. 
2.  For node support poles: No later than 150 business days after the date the City receives the complete application. 
3.  For transport facilities: No later than 21 business days after the City receives the complete application. 
(c)  Basis for denial of application. If the City denies an application, it shall document the basis for the denial, including the specific applicable City code provisions or other City rules, regulations, or other law on which the denial is based. The documentation for the denial must be sent by electronic mail to the applicant on or before the date that the City Administrator denies the application. 
(d)  Resubmission of denied application. The applicant may cure the deficiencies identified in the denial application. 
1.  The applicant has 30 business days from the date the City denies the completed application to cure the deficiencies identified in the denial documentation and resubmit the application without paying an additional application fee, other than any fee for actual costs incurred by the City. 
2.  The City shall approve or deny the resubmitted and completed application after a denial not later than the 90th business day after the date the City receives the resubmitted and completed application. The City's review of the resubmitted application shall be limited to the deficiencies cited in the denial documentation. 
3.  Business day means Monday through Friday, excepting local, state or federal holidays. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-54. - Exceptions to permit requirement; Notice requirement. 
(a)  A network provider is not required to obtain a construction permit, or pay a rate to the City for: 
1.  Routine maintenance that does not require excavation or closing of sidewalks or vehicular lanes in a public right-of-way; 
2.  Replacing or upgrading a network node or network pole with a node or pole that is substantially similar in size or smaller and that does not require excavation or closing of sidewalks or vehicular lanes in a public right-of-way; or 
3.  The installation, placement, maintenance, operation, or replacement of micro network nodes that are strung on cables between existing poles or node support poles in compliance with the National Electrical Safety Code. 
(b)  At least 24-hour advance written notice to the City of work performed under this section is required, including proof that the network provider is acting with approval of a facility/pole's owner; and proof that the size limitations may not in any event exceed the parameters prescribed by this article and the City's Design Manual. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-55. - Fees. 
(a)  Network Provider Fees. 
1.  Annual network node user fee/network node rate for right-of-way use. Network providers shall pay the City an annual network node user fee for each location for which network provider has obtained permit(s) for the installation of network nodes, regardless of whether or not a network provider installs network nodes in the public right-of-way. The amount of the annual network node user fee shall be set by resolution in the City's Centralized/Master Fee Schedule. The annual network node user fee payment for the first year at any location begins accruing when the permit is issued and is due 30 days after network provider obtains a permit to install or collocate a network node at the location. 
(i)  The initial annual network node user fee shall be pro-rated for the months remaining in the calendar year after the permit issuance date. 
(ii)  The annual network node user fee for every year after the initial annual network node payment shall be paid in advance on or before January 1st of each calendar year for each network node in the public right-of-way for the next calendar year period. 
(iii)  Annual network node user fee adjustment. The City may adjust the annual network node user fee by an amount equal to one-half the annual change in the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers for Texas, as published by the federal Bureau of Labor Statistics. The City shall provide written notice to each network provider of the new rate, and the new rate shall apply to the first payment due to the City on or after the 60th day following the City's notice. 
2.  Annual collocation on city service pole attachment fee. Network providers shall pay the City an annual collocation on City service pole fee for each network node permitted to be collocated on a City service pole for each location for which network provider has obtained permit(s) to co-locate a network node on a service pole, regardless of whether or not a network provider collocates a network node on a service pole. The amount of the annual collocation on City service pole fee shall be set by resolution in the City's Centralized/Master Fee Schedule. Payment for the first year at any service pole location begins accruing when the permit is issued and is due 30 days after network provider obtains a permit to install or collocate a network node at the service pole location. 
(i)  The initial annual collocation on City service pole fee shall be pro-rated for the months remaining in the calendar year after the permit issuance date. 
(ii)  The annual collocation on City service pole fee for every year after the initial annual network node payment shall be paid in advance on or before January 1st of each calendar year for each network node collocated in the public right-of-way for the next calendar year. 
3.  Monthly transport facility user fee. Network providers shall pay the City a monthly transport facility user fee for each network node located in the public right-of-way, which shall be paid on a quarterly basis, in the amount set by resolution in the City's Centralized/Master Fee Schedule, which begins accruing when the permit is issued. This monthly transport facility user fee is in addition to any annual network node user fee/network node annual rental rate for use of the public right-of-way as required by Chapter 284, Section 284.053, as amended. 
4.  Network node application fee. Network provider shall pay the City the application fees set by resolution in the City's Centralized/Master Fee Schedule contemporaneously with the submittal of the application for the permit(s). 
5.  No other fees. The City shall not charge a network provider any other fees or seek payment for any other compensation, other than the fees and compensation provided for in this section as authorized by Chapter 284, as may be amended. 
(b)  Annexation and disannexation. Within 30 days following the date of the passage of any action effecting the annexation of any property to or the disannexation of any property from the City's corporate boundaries, the City agrees to furnish user written notice of the action and an accurate map of the City's corporate boundaries showing, if available, street names and number details. For the purpose of compensating the City under this article, a permit holder shall start including or excluding facilities within the affected area in the permit holder's count of facilities within 30 days of receipt of the City's notice of the annexation or disannexation. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-56. - Design manual and certificates of operation. 
(a)  Compliance with design manual. A network provider shall comply with the City's Design Manual for the Installation of Network Nodes and Node Support Poles, as amended. 
(b)  Certificates of operation. 
1.  As part of the application process for the installation of network nodes, the network provider must certify that the proposed network node will be placed into active commercial service by or for a network provider no later than the 60th day after the date the construction and final testing of the network node is completed. 
2.  An updated certification of active service must be submitted annually, by no later than December 31st, with or prior to payment of the applicable annual fee(s). 
3.  If the network provider is not in active commercial service for a period in excess of 60 consecutive days, the equipment will be deemed abandoned and the permit will be revoked. The network provider will be required, within 90 days from notification from the City, to remove the equipment at the network provider's sole expense. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-57. - Violations and Penalty. 
    The penalty provisions in section 34-47 of this article shall apply to this division. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-58. - Conflicts with other requirements. 
    Where this Division conflicts with any other provision of the City Code of Ordinances, this division shall control. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
DIVISION 3. - REGULATIONS APPLICABLE TO ALL USERS OF THE CITY'S PUBLIC RIGHT-OF-WAY 

Sec. 34-59. - Additional requirements applicable to all users. 
    The following provisions apply to any person, provider, network provider, telecommunications provider or user performing any construction, installation or other work in the public right-of-way, whether under a permit issued under this article or otherwise: 
(a)  Specifications. All excavations, alterations, backfill, repairs, and other work in or on the public right-of-way must be made in conformance with any written specifications or requirements adopted by the City. The City Administrator, the Supervisor or the City engineer may allow modifications of a specification if unusual circumstances are present, the modifications will comply with the spirit and intent of the specification, and the modification will not adversely affect the public safety or welfare. All work must be performed in a good and workmanlike manner and in accordance with all applicable federal, state, and local laws, and rules and regulations. 
(b)  Boring and encasing. If the City Administrator or Supervisor determines it is impractical to excavate within a street, all pipelines, conduits, or other crossings must be bored, tunneled, or drilled under the paved section, and, if required by the City Administrator or Supervisor, the crossings must be encased in a manner approved by the City Administrator or his/her designee. 
(c)  Damage to city streets. Any type of ditching equipment used on City streets must be equipped with street pads. All damage done to public right-of-way and other public property during the work must be repaired by the permit holder to City specifications. If the permit holder fails to make the repairs, the City Administrator may make the repairs and charge the cost to the permit holder. 
(d)  Correction of Defects. If a permit holder fails to properly restore the surface of the public right-of-way or other public property, abandons the work, or fails to correct a hazardous condition after notice to do so, the City Administrator may take any action necessary to restore the right-of-way, complete the work, or correct the hazardous condition at the permit holder's sole expense. 
1.  A permit holder shall restore and repair the rights-of-way from any damage to the rights-of-way, or any facilities located within the rights-of-way, and the property of any third party resulting from permit holder's removal or relocation activities, or any other of permit holder's activities under this article, in strict accordance with the City's Code of Ordinances, and other applicable laws, except to the extent not consistent with Chapter 284. 
2.  A permit holder shall repair any damage to the rights-of-way, or any facilities located within the rights-of-way, and the property of any third party resulting from permit holder's removal or relocation activities, or any other of permit holder's activities under this article, within ten calendar days following the date of such removal or relocation, at permit holder's sole cost and expense, including restoration of the rights-of-way and such property to substantially the same condition as it was immediately before the date permit holder was granted a permit for the applicable location or did the work at such location (even if the person did not first obtain a permit), including restoration or replacement of any damaged trees, shrubs or other vegetation. Such repair, restoration and replacement shall be subject to the sole, reasonable approval of the City Administrator. 
(e)  Debris on public rights-of-way. During the work, the public right-of-way must be kept clean of excessive rubbish, earth, mud, rock, and other debris, to the satisfaction of the City Administrator. 
(f)  Traffic safety. All work in a public right-of-way or adjacent to a street must be done with barricades, traffic cones, lights, flares, signs, flagmen, and other traffic control devices as specified in the latest edition of the MUTCD of the Texas Department of Transportation. Where the City Administrator or his/her designee believes it is necessary to avoid traffic congestion or for public safety, the City Administrator may require work be done only at certain hours during the day or night. Any excavation in the public right- of-way that is a potential danger to the public must be secured against entry in the manner specified by the City Administrator or his/her designee. 
(g)  Inspection. The City Administrator, Supervisor or their designee and applicable code enforcement officer may inspect the work to determine whether the facilities are being or have been constructed in compliance with this article, applicable codes, other applicable ordinances, and state law. The owner of the facilities must correct work that is not in compliance with the foregoing requirements. 
(h)  As-built maps and records. The facility owner, network provider, or user shall maintain accurate maps and other appropriate records of its facilities as they are actually constructed in the rights-of-way, including, upon request, the use of Auto CAD/GIS digital format. Facility owner, network provider or user will provide additional maps to the City upon request. 
(i)  Ownership. A facility owner's, network provider's or user's facilities erected or placed in or on the public right-of-way shall not be considered to be affixed to or part of the public right-of-way. All such facilities will be and remain the property of the facility owner, network provider and may be removed by the facility owner, network provider at any time, provided that the facility owner, network provider or user must notify the City Administrator prior to any work in the public right-of-way; and removal is performed in strict accordance with all applicable City ordinances, state and federal laws. 
(j)  Tree maintenance. The owner of facilities, network provider or user in the public right-of-way must obtain written permission from the City Administrator before trimming trees hanging over the City's facilities, or its facilities to prevent branches from contacting the City's facilities or its facilities. When directed by the City Administrator, the owner of the facilities, network provider or user shall trim the trees under the supervision and direction of the City's inspector or his/her designee. The City will not be liable for any damages, injuries, or claims arising the owner's actions under this subsection. 
(k)  Graffiti abatement. As soon as practicable but not later than 14 calendar days from receipt of written notice from the City, the owner of facilities, network provider or user in the public right-of-way shall remove all graffiti on its facilities located in the public right-of-way. The foregoing shall not relieve the owner of facilities, network provider or user from complying with any City graffiti or visual blight ordinance or regulation. 
(l)  Drug policy. It is the policy of the City to achieve a drug-free workforce and workplace. The manufacture, distribution, dispensation, possession, sale or use of illegal drugs or alcohol by facility owner's, network providers, user's employees, contractors, subcontractors, or vendors while on City premises, including the public rights-of-way, is prohibited. 
(m)  Minimize ground equipment density. In accordance with Chapter 284, Section 284.102(1) to enhance the safety requirements of line of sight of pedestrians, particularly small children, the City Administrator may deny a request for a proposed location if the network provider installs network node ground equipment where existing ground equipment within 300 feet already occupies a footprint of 25 square feet or more. 
(n)  Concealment. Facilities, including but not limited to network node facilities, shall be concealed or enclosed as much as reasonably possible in an equipment box, cabinet, or other unit that may include ventilation openings. External cables and wires hanging off a pole shall be sheathed or enclosed in a conduit, and positioned on the pole in a manner hidden from view of the street to the extent practical, so that wires are protected and not visible or visually minimized to the extent possible in strict accordance with the City's rights-of-way management ordinance, and other applicable ordinances, except to the extent not consistent with Chapter 284. 
(o)  Minimize ground equipment concentration. In order to minimize negative visual impact to the surrounding area, and in accordance with Chapter 284, Section 284.102(1) to enhance the safety requirements of line of sight of pedestrians, particularly small children, the City Administrator may deny a request for a proposed location if the network provider installs network node ground equipment where existing ground equipment within 300 feet already occupies a footprint of 25 square feet or more to minimize effect on property values and aesthetics on the area. 
(p)  Allowed colors. Colors in historic districts and historic areas and design districts must be approved by the City Administrator from a palette of approved colors. Unless otherwise provided, all colors shall be earth tones or shall match the background of any structure the facilities are located upon and all efforts shall be made for the colors to be inconspicuous. Colors in areas other than in historic districts and historic areas and design districts shall conform to colors of other installations of telecommunication providers in the immediately adjacent areas. 
(q)  Interference not permitted. A facility owner, network provider or user shall operate all facilities in accordance with all applicable laws, including regulations adopted by the Federal Communications Commission. A facility owner, network provider shall ensure that the operation of its facilities does not cause any harmful radio frequency interference to a Federal Communications Commission-authorized mobile telecommunications operation of the City operating at the time the facilities were initially installed or constructed. On written notice by the City, a facility owner, network provider or user shall take all steps reasonably necessary to remedy any harmful interference. If a facility owner, network provider or user fails to correct any harmful interference within 60 days of written notice, the City may upon 14 day advance written notice revoke any and all permits for the facilities. 
(r)  Cable service not authorized by permit. A permit holder is not authorized to provide cable service as a cable operator in the City under this article, but must first obtain a franchise agreement from the City for that purpose, under such terms and conditions as may be required by law. A permit for the installation, placement, maintenance, or operation of a network node or transport facility under this article shall not confer authorization to provide cable service or video service, as defined by V.T.C.A., Section 66.002, Utilities Code, or information service as defined by 47 U.S.C. Section 153(24), or wireless service as defined by 47 U.S.C. Section 153(53), in the public right-of-way. 
(s)  Signage. Permit holder, facility owner, network provider or user shall post its name, location identifying information, and emergency telephone number in an area on the cabinet of the facility that is visible to the public. Signage required under Chapter 284 shall not exceed four inches by six inches, unless otherwise required by law (e.g. RF ground notification signs) or the City Administrator. Except as required by law or by the utility pole owner, no other signs or advertising shall be posted on the facility, micro network node, network node, node support pole, service pole or utility pole. 
(t)  Permit rights apply to permit holder only. The rights granted by this article inure to the benefit of the permit holder only. The rights granted by permit may not be assigned, transferred, or sold to another person by the permit holder. For the purposes of this article, assignment, transfer or sale means a change of operating control of the permit holder, expressly excepting an assignment or transfer to entities that control, are controlled by or are under common control with permit holder. 
(u)  Deed restrictions. Any person, provider, user, network provider, facility owner installing facilities in a public right-of way shall comply with private deed restrictions and other private restrictions in the area. 
(v)  Courtesy and proper performance. Any person, provider, user, network provider, facility owner shall make citizen satisfaction a priority in using the rights-of-way. The person, provider, user, network provider, facility owner shall train its employees to be customer service-oriented and to positively and politely interact with citizens when dealing with issues pertaining to its facilities in the rights-of-way. The person's, provider's, user's, network provider's, facility owner's employees shall be clean, courteous, efficient, and neat in appearance and committed to offering the highest quality of interaction with the public. If, in the opinion of the City Administrator or his/her designee, the person, provider, user, network provider, facility owner is not interacting in a positive and polite manner with citizens, he or she shall request that person, provider, user, network provider, facility owner to take all remedial steps to conform to these standards. 
(w)  On or before January 1st of each year, or within 30 days of a change in the contact information, an owner of facilities, network provider or user in the public right-of-way must update its contact information, to include the name, address, telephone number and e-mail address of the person to whom the City may provide notices. If the person fails to provide the updated contact information, any notices that are sent shall be considered valid if sent to the name and address of the person on file with the City. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-60. - Construction standards applicable to all users. 
(a)  Advance notice required. The City Administrator or his/her designee shall be notified 24 hours in advance that construction is ready to proceed by either the right-of-way user, their contractor or representative, including the name, address, and phone numbers of the contractor performing the actual construction, and the name and telephone number of the individual who will be available at all times during construction. Failure to provide the above information will result in the suspension of the permit until the required information is received. 
(b)  Conformance to other laws. All construction shall be in conformance with all City codes and applicable local, state, and federal laws. 
(c)  Erosion control. Erosion control measures (i.e., silt fence) and advance warning signs, markers, cones, and barricades must be in place before work begins. Permit holder may be required to show proof of EPA approved plans relating to storm water and erosion when applicable or a letter stating such plans are not required. User shall comply with City, state, and federal guidelines regulating storm water management erosion control. Requirements shall include, but not be limited to, silt fencing around any excavation that will be left overnight, silt fencing in erosion areas until reasonable vegetation is established, barricade fencing around open holes, and high erosion areas will require wire backed silt fencing, or straw bales, as appropriate. 
(d)  Lane closures. In the interest of the public safety, the City Administrator or his/her designee may determine that lane closures on collectors, thoroughfares, and streets will be limited to certain hours and/or times of the day. Arrow boards will be required on lane closures, with all barricades, advanced warning signs and thirty-six-inch reflector cones placed according to the specifications of the City Administrator or his/her designee. 
(e)  Workmanship. Users are responsible for the workmanship and any damages caused by a contractor or subcontractor. A responsible representative of the permit holder will be available to City Administrator or his/her designee at all times during construction. 
(f)  Notice of damage. All users shall notify the City Administrator or his/her designee immediately of any damage to other utilities, either City or privately owned. 
(g)  Prior approval required for street or sidewalk cut. Except in an emergency, prior approval must be obtained from the City Administrator or his/her designee when a street or sidewalk cut is required and all requirements of the City shall be followed. Repair of all street and sidewalk removals shall be made promptly to avoid safety hazards to vehicle and pedestrian traffic. 
(h)  Interference prohibited. Newly installed structures shall not interfere with facilities or structures of other users, in particular gravity dependent facilities. 
(i)  Working hours. Except in an emergency, working hours in the rights-of-way are 7:00 a.m. to 7:00 p.m., Monday through Saturday. Work that needs to be performed after 7:00 p.m. Monday through Saturday must be approved in advance. Except in an emergency, any work performed on Sunday must be approved at least 24 hours in advance by the City Administrator or his/her designee. Directional boring is permitted only Monday through Friday, unless approved in advance. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-61. - Plans of record. 
    Right-of-way users shall provide the City Administrator or his/her designee with "plans of record" within ten days of completion of structures in the right-of-way. The plans shall be provided to the City in the format specified by the City Administrator or his/her designee. Submittal of "plans of record" should be in digital formatting as well as written or in any other format requested by the City Administrator or his/her designee. The requirement to provide "plans of record" may be waived by the City Administrator or his/her designee upon a showing of good cause. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-62. - Facility location and conformance with public improvements. 
    Prior to initiating construction of a "City project" in the right-of-way, the City will provide each right-of-way user preliminary project plans at various stages of completion (i.e., 30 percent plans, 60 percent plans, 90 percent plans and final plans). Upon receipt of the first submittal of preliminary project plans (30 percent plans), each right-of-way user shall be responsible for verifying the location of its underground structures in the vicinity of the City's project. In verifying the location of structures as required by this section, each right-of-way user shall compile the information obtained regarding any structures located in the right-of-way that are potentially affected by the City project and shall, within 30 days of receipt of the first submittal of the preliminary project plans, make that information available to the City in a written and verified format acceptable to the City Administrator or his/her designee. Whenever by reasons of widening or straightening of streets, water or sewer line projects, or any other City projects (i.e., install or improve storm drains, water lines, sewer lines) it shall be deemed necessary by the City Council to remove, alter, change, adapt, or conform the underground or overhead structures of a right-of-way user, such alterations shall be made by the owner of the structures at the owner's expense within 45 calendar days from the receipt of written notice to make the alterations, unless a different schedule has been approved by the City Administrator or his/her designee. The owner of the structures shall be responsible for any direct costs incurred by the City, associated with project delays resulting from owner's failure to conform structures within the time limits established by this section. Reimbursement for all costs provided for by this section shall be paid the City within 30 calendar days from the day which the owner receives written notice or an invoice of the costs. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Sec. 34-63. - Improperly installed facilities or structures. 
(a)  Proper installation required. Facilities or structures in the rights-of-way shall be properly installed, repaired, upgraded and maintained. Facilities or structures shall be considered to be improperly installed, repaired, upgraded, or maintained if: 
1.  The installation, repairs, upgrade, or maintenance endangers people; 
2.  The facilities or structures do not meet the applicable City requirements; 
3.  The facilities or structures are not capable of being located using standard practices; or 
4.  The facilities or structures are not located in the proper place in accordance with the plans approved by the City Administrator or his/her designee. 
(b)  Existing structures. This section shall not apply to facilities or structures installed prior to the effective date of this ordinance unless such facilities or structures are repaired or upgraded. 
(c)  City administrator review of poles. When poles are used, the type of poles, location, depth, upgrades, and other specifications shall be subject to review of the City Administrator or his/her designee, unless otherwise provided by this article. 
(Ord. No. 17-11, § 3, 9-12-2017) 
Secs. 34-64-34-65. - Reserved. 
Chapter 36 - SUBDIVISIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Regulation of subdivision and property development, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 212. 

Sec. 36-1. - Authority. 
    This chapter is adopted under the authority of the constitution and laws of the state, including particularly V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 212, and the provisions of the Municipal Annexation Act, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 43. 
(Code 1981, § 17.1; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.1) 
Sec. 36-2. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this chapter is to provide for the orderly, safe and healthful development of the area within the City, and within the area surrounding the City and to promote the health, safety, morals and general welfare of the community. 
(Code 1981, § 17.2; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.2) 
Sec. 36-3. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. Definitions not expressly prescribed herein are to be construed in accordance with customary usage in municipal planning and engineering practices. 
    Alley means a minor public right-of-way, not intended to provide the primary means of access to abutting lots, which is used primarily for vehicular service access to the back or sides of properties otherwise abutting on a street. 
    Engineer means the person duly authorized under the provisions of the Texas Engineering Registration Act, as heretofore or hereafter amended, to practice the profession of engineering. 
    Lot means an undivided tract or parcel of land having frontage on a public street and which: 
(1)  Is, or in the future may be offered for sale, conveyance, transfer or improvement; 
(2)  Is designated as a district and separate tract; and 
(3)  Is identified by a tract or lot number or symbol in a duly approved subdivision plat which has been properly filed of record. 
    Pavement width means the portion of a street available for vehicular traffic; where curbs are laid; it is the portion between the faces of curbs. 
    Streets means a public right-of-way, however designated, which provides vehicular access to adjacent land. 
    Subdivider means any person or any agent thereof, dividing or proposing to divide land so as to constitute a subdivision as that term is defined herein. Without limitation the term "subdivider" shall include the owner, equitable owner or authorized agent of such owner or equitable owner, of land sought to be subdivided. 
    Subdivision means a division of land within the City limits or in the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the City, that divides the tract in two or more parts to lay out a subdivision of the tract, including an addition to the City, to lay out suburban, building, or other lots, or to lay out streets, alleys, squares, parks, or other parts of the tract intended to be dedicated to public use or for the use of purchasers or owners of lots fronting on or adjacent to the streets, alleys, squares, parks, or other parts. A division of a tract under this definition includes a division regardless of whether it is made by using a metes and bounds description in a deed of conveyance or in a contract for a deed, by using a contract of sale or other executory contract to convey, or by using any other method. A division of land under this definition does not include a division of land into parts greater than five acres, where each part has access and no public improvement is being dedicated. 
    Surveyor means a licensed state land surveyor or a registered public surveyor, as authorized by the state statutes to practice the profession of surveying. 
    Utility easement means an interest in land granted to the City, to the public generally, or to a private utility corporation, for installing or maintaining utilities across, over or under land, together with the right to enter thereon with machinery and vehicles necessary for the maintenance of said utilities. 
(Code 1981, § 17.3; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.3) 
Sec. 36-4. - Special provisions. 
(a)  Septic tank permits. No permit shall be issued by the City for the installation of a septic tank upon any lot in any subdivision for which a final plat has not been approved and filed for record, or upon any lot in a subdivision in which the standards contained herein or referred to herein have not been complied with in full. 
(b)  Building or repair permits. No building or repair permit shall be issued by the City for any structure on a lot in a subdivision for which a final plat has not been approved and filed for record, not for any structure on a lot within a subdivision opened after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived in which the standards contained herein or referred to herein have not been complied with in full. 
(c)  Maintenance by City. The City shall not repair, maintain, install or provide any streets or public utility services in any subdivision for which a final plat has not been approved and filed for record, nor in which the standards contained herein or referred to herein have not been complied with in full. This subsection (c) shall not apply to streets or public utility services being maintained by the City on the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived. 
(d)  Utilities. Except insofar as to complete the building of the subdivision the City, utility companies, corporations or individuals shall not sell or supply any water, gas, electricity or sewerage service within a subdivision for which a final plat has not been approved or filed for record, nor in which the standards contained herein or referred to herein have not been complied with in full. No such service shall be afforded any subdivision for which no preliminary plat has been filed. 
(e)  Enforcement. In behalf of the City, the City Attorney shall, when directed by the City Council, institute appropriate action in a court of competent jurisdiction to enforce the provisions of this chapter or the standards referred to herein with respect to any violation thereof which occurs within the City, within the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the City as such jurisdiction as determined under the Municipal Annexation Act, or within any area subject to all or part of the provisions of this chapter. 
(f)  Noncompliance; recordation. If any subdivision for which a final plat has not been approved is opened after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived, and the City Council shall pass a resolution reciting the fact of such a noncompliance or failure to secure final plat approval, the City Secretary shall, when directed by the City Council, cause a certified copy of such resolution under the corporate seal of the City to be filed in the deed records of the county or counties in which such subdivision or part thereof lies. If full compliance and final plat approval are secured after the filing of such resolution, the City Secretary shall forthwith file an instrument in the deed of records of such county or counties stating that this chapter is no longer violated. 
(Code 1981, § 17.4; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.4) 
Sec. 36-5. - Variances. 
    The City Council may authorize a variance from these regulations when, in its opinion, undue hardship will result from requiring strict compliance. In granting a variance, the City Council shall prescribe such conditions that it deems necessary to or desirable in the public interest. 
(Code 1981, § 17.5; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.5) 
Sec. 36-6. - Preliminary conference. 
    Prior to the official filing of a preliminary plat, the subdivider should consult with and present a proposed plan of subdivision to the mayor or the mayor's designate for comments and advice on the procedures, specifications and standards required by the City for the subdivision of land. 
(Code 1981, § 17.6; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.6) 
Sec. 36-7. - Plat requirements and procedure. 
(a)  Filing fees. Each preliminary plat or final plat submitted shall be accompanied by a filing fee as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the City Council from time to time. Both fees shall be applied to replats or a preliminary and final that are submitted at the same time. No action by the City in accepting or approving any plat or plans shall be valid until the filing fee has been paid. This fee shall not be refunded for any plat that is withdrawn or disapproved. 
(b)  Preliminary plat. 
(1)  Following the pre-submission conference required by section 36-6, all persons desiring to subdivide a tract of land into a subdivision as defined in section 36-3 shall first prepare and submit to the City a preliminary plat not less than ten days prior to the date at which formal application for the preliminary plat approval is made to the City Council. 
(2)  The following information on the preliminary plat shall be certified by a state registered professional civil engineer or by a state licensed or registered land surveyor: Seven copies of the preliminary plat showing the general features of the proposed development. This preliminary plat shall be drawn on a scale of 200 feet to the inch or larger (100 feet to the inch preferred) and shall show the following: 
a.  The outline of the tract the plat is proposed to subdivide with principal dimensions. 
b.  The proposed plan of subdivision, showing streets, blocks, lots, alleys, squares, easements, building lines, and parks, with principal dimensions. The preliminary plat shall cover all of the tract intended to be developed, at any time, even though it is intended by the developers or developer to file plats and install improvements for parts of said tract by section or unit. 
c.  The location, width and name of existing streets and any blocks, lots, alleys, easements, building lines and water courses or other natural features in the affected with principal dimensions and any other significant information on all sides for a distance of not less than 200 feet. 
d.  The names of proposed streets. Such names shall conform to the names of existing streets of which they may be or become extensions or otherwise shall not duplicate or conflict with the recognized name of any other street located in the area subject to these regulations. 
e.  The location of existing sewers, water and gas mains and other public utilities, if any. 
f.  A general plan of the stormwater drainage sufficiently detailed to indicate the location of drainage ditches or structures and the direction of flow. 
g.  The name of the proposed subdivision, north point, scale and date. 
h.  The name of the owner or owners and the engineer or surveyor. 
i.  Vicinity sketch or key map at a scale of not more than 800 feet to the inch which shall show all existing subdivisions, streets and tracts of acreage in the area and the general drainage plan, ultimate designation of water and possible storm sewer connections by arrows. 
j.  Typical cross section of the street improvements proposed by the professional engineer. 
k.  Topographical contours of not more than five-foot intervals. 
l.  The original boundary survey of the tract of land to be subdivided, which shall close within one in 10,000 (1:10,000). The original closure calculations for the closure will be furnished with the preliminary plat. Linear dimensions shall be expressed in feet and decimals of a foot; angular dimensions may be shown in bearings. Curved boundaries shall be fully described and all essential information given; circular shall be defined by degree of curve. The subdivision boundary lines be indicated by heavy lines and the computed acreage of the subdivision will be shown on the preliminary plat. 
m.  A number or letter to identify each lot or site and each block. 
n.  A copy of any and all restrictions certified by the subdivider applying to this subdivision only. 
(c)  Processing of preliminary plat. 
(1)  Within 30 days after the preliminary plat is formally filed, the City Council shall conditionally approve or disapprove such plat or conditionally approve it with modifications. If it is conditionally disapproved or conditionally approved with modifications, the City Council shall inform the subdivider of the reasons at the time such action is taken. 
(2)  Conditional approval of a preliminary plat shall be effective for a period of six months unless reviewed by the City Council in the light of new significant information (whether or not available to the City Council at the time the preliminary plat was approved) which would necessitate a revision of the preliminary plat. If the City Council should deem changes in a preliminary plat as necessary, it shall use the layout submitted on the preliminary plat as a guide to the installation of streets, water, sewer and other required improvements and utilities and to the preparation of the final or recorded plat. Conditional approval of a preliminary plat shall not constitute automatic approval of the final plat. 
(Code 1981, § 17.7; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.7) 
Sec. 36-8. - Final plat forms and content. 
(a)  The final plat shall conform to the preliminary plat as conditionally approved by the City Council incorporating any and all changes, modifications, alterations, corrections and conditions imposed by the City Council. This plat shall be drawn to a scale of one inch equals 100 feet, or larger in ink or linen cloth with all figures and letters legible and the whole proper for filing for record in the office of the county clerk. The plat shall be on a 22 inches by 32 inches sheet of linen cloth. 
(b)  The final plat shall also include the following: 
(1)  Owner's Dedication and Acknowledgment. 
THE STATE OF TEXAS 
COUNTY OF VAN ZANDT 
    I (We), the undersigned, owner(s) of the land shown on this plat, and designated herein as the ____________ / ____________ / ____________ subdivision to the City of Wills Point, Texas, and whose name is subscribed hereto, hereby dedicate and grant, sell and convey to the use of the City of Wills Point, Texas, forever all streets, alleys, parks, water courses, drains, easements and public places hereon shown for the purpose and consideration therein expressed. 
____________ Owner  
THE STATE OF TEXAS COUNTY OF VAN ZANDT 
    Before me, the undersigned authority, on this day personally appeared ____________ known to me to be the person whose name is subscribed to the foregoing instrument, and acknowledged to me that the person executed the same for the purpose and consideration therein stated. 
    Given under my hand and seal of office this ____________ day of ____________ , 20 ____________ . 
____________ ____________ NOTARY PUBLIC IN AND FOR VAN 
ZANDT COUNTY, TEXAS  
(SEAL) 
(2)  Approval of the City Council. 
STATE OF TEXAS 
COUNTY OF VAN ZANDT 
CITY OF WILLS POINT 
    On this the ____________ day of ____________ / ____________ / ____________ , 20 ____________ , this plat is hereby approved by the City Council. 
____________ Mayor  
ATTEST: 
____________ / ____________ / ____________ 
City Secretary 
(3)  Certification of the Survey. 
THE STATE OF TEXAS 
COUNTY OF VAN ZANDT 
    I, the undersigned, a (registered professional engineer/public surveyor) in the State of Texas, hereby certify that this plat is true and correct and was prepared from an actual survey of the property made under my supervision on the ground. 
____________ ____________ Registered Professional Engineer or 
Registered Public Surveyor  
(Engineer or Surveyor's Seal) 
In addition to the foregoing the owner shall execute such further documents, including without limitation, deeds of dedication, as the City in its discretion shall desire to effectuate the transfer to the City. 
(c)  The original and seven copies of the final plat shall be submitted. The final plat shall contain all of the following: 
(1)  The plat shall have the title or name by which the subdivision is to be identified, north point, the scale of the map, and the name of the civil engineer or land surveyor responsible. 
(2)  A definite legal description and identification of the tract being subdivided. This description shall be sufficient for the requirements of title examination. The plat shall be a descriptive diagram drawn to scale, and shall show by reference that the subdivision is a particular portion or part of a previously filed plat or recognized grant or partition, which diagram and description shall show as being included in the subdivision, at least all of the smallest unit or the last filed subdivision, plat or grant, out of which the instant subdivision is divided, or so much thereof as is owned by the subdivider. 
(3)  The boundaries of the subdivided property, the location or designation of all streets, alleys, parks and other areas intended to be dedicated or deeded to the public use, with proper dimensions. The boundaries of the subdivision shall be indicated by a heavy line and shall be tied by dimension to the established center line of all existing boundary streets. 
(4)  The location of all adjacent streets and alleys, with their names and the names of adjoining subdivisions with exact location and designation by number of lots and blocks. 
(5)  All lots, block and street boundary lines, with blocks and lots numbered or lettered consecutively. Building lines and easements shall be shown and shall be defined by dimension. The actual width of all streets shall be shown, measured at right angles or radially, where curved. All principal lines shall have the bearing and any deviations from the norm shall be indicated. 
(6)  Accurate dimensions, both linear and angular, of all items on the plat; the boundary survey on the site shall close within one in 10,000 (1:10,000). Linear dimensions shall be expressed in feet and decimals of a foot; angular dimensions may be shown by bearings. Curved boundaries shall be fully described and all essential information given; circular curves shall be defined by actual length of radius and not by degree or curve. Complete dimensional data shall be given on fractional lots. The plat shall denote five-foot contour lines as established from the U.S. Coast and Geodetic Survey datum. 
(7)  The location and description of all lot and block corners and permanent survey reference monuments. Such corners and monuments shall be of three-quarter inch iron pipe or five-eighths inch iron rod and shall meet the following standards: 
a.  Lot corners shall be 24 inches to 30 inches long with the top of the iron pipe or iron rod set flush with the finished grade of the ground. 
b.  Block corners shall be 24 inches to 30 inches long with the top of the iron pipe or iron rod set flush with finished grade of the ground and shall include the beginning and end of all curves within each block. 
c.  Reference point shall be 24 inches to 30 inches long placed one foot below the surface of the finished ground elevation at suitable locations throughout the subdivision. There shall be at least as many reference points as there are blocks in the subdivision but not less than two, and the distance between successive monuments along any street or reference line shall not be greater than 1,000 feet. Reference points shall be other than and in addition to markers set for blocks or lot corners. 
d.  A certificate of ownership in fee of all land embraced in the subdivision, and of the authenticity of the plat and dedication, signed and acknowledged by all owners of any interest in said land. The acknowledgment shall be in the form required in the conveyance of real estate. Approval and acceptance of all lien holders shall be included. 
e.  A certificate by the responsible surveyor or engineer in charge, duly authenticated, that the plat is true and correct and in accordance with the determination of surveys actually made on the ground. If the surveyor or engineer who prepared the plat did not make the boundary survey, this fact should be noted in the certificate. Also, the certificate should show whether or not the tract is within five miles of the City limits, measured in a straight line from the nearest points in the City limits, unless the information is shown in suitable manner elsewhere on the face of the plat. 
f.  The final plat submitted to the City Council and to be filed for record with the county clerk shall show construction features such as curb lines or public utility lines, including without limitation water, sewer, gas and electrical easements, or other structures not involved in the title covenant, and shall conform with the legal requirements for plats found in V.T.C.A., Property Code § 12.002. 
(Code 1981, § 17.8; Ord. of 3-12-1979, § 17.8) 
Sec. 36-9. - Standards and specifications. 
    No preliminary or final plat shall be approved by the City Council unless they conform to the following standards: 
(1)  Generally. 
a.  Conformity. The subdivision shall conform to the overall plans of the City. 
b.  Provisions for future subdivisions. If tract is subdivided into parcels larger than ordinary building lots, such parcels shall be arranged to allow the opening of future streets. 
(2)  Streets. 
a.
